10062-8{_}3554{_}It was pointed out that Vincent and Rosa had been educated in the North; that Mrs. Atterbury had spent many of her recent summers there.
10062-8{_}3555{_}Their devotion to the Confederacy must be shown by deeds.
10062-8{_}3556{_}It was true they had given twenty thousand dollars to the cause, but what was that to threefold millionaires?
10062-8{_}3557{_}General Lee, their kinsman, had shaken his Socratic head solemnly when Rosa, at the War Department, told him, as an excellent joke, the strange chance that had brought Vincent's college chum and his family under the kind Rosedale roof.
10062-8{_}3558{_}Richard Perley was, therefore, deputized to rescue Barney from his false position and give him a chance for exchange when the time came.
10062-8{_}3559{_}He journeyed up to Richmond, and, one day, laid these facts before Barney, who instantly saw his friend's dilemma, and at once set about inventing a _ruse_ that should extricate him, without mortifying the kind people who had befriended him.
10062-8{_}3560{_}When he was able to be about, he feigned a desire to go to his friends in Arrowfield County, south of the James, and was bidden hearty Godspeed.
10062-8{_}3561{_}Then, with funds supplied by Jack, he gained admittance to a modest house far out on Main Street, where the city merges into the country.
10062-8{_}3562{_}They were simple people, and his thrilling tale of being a refugee from Harper's Ferry was plausible enough to be accepted by more skeptical people than the Gannats.
10062-8{_}3563{_}Day after day Barney skirted furtively about the uncompromising walls of Libby and Castle Thunder, where once or twice he had gone with his hosts to make a mental diagram of the place for future use.
10062-8{_}3564{_}Little by little he became familiar with Richmond, which, like a new bride, gave the visitor welcome to admire her splendid spouse, the Confederate government.
10062-8{_}3565{_}He learned all the plots of the prison, and became the confidant of Letitia Lanview, known to every exile in Richmond as the friend of the suffering--St. Veronica she was called--after a poem dedicated to her by a young Harvard graduate, rescued by her perseverance from death in Libby Prison.
10062-8{_}3566{_}With this lady he drove all about the environs of Richmond, and several times far out toward the meditated route of flight, in order that he might be able to lead the bewildered refugees.
10062-8{_}3567{_}He got the whole landscape by heart, and could have led a battalion over it in the dark.
10062-8{_}3568{_}Then he passed days wandering over the Libby Hill, down in the bed of the "Rockets," as the bed of the James was known in those days; he learned the ground to the very beat of the patrols that guarded the wretched prisoners in the towering shambles.
10062-8{_}3569{_}One whole night, too, he spent in marking the course of the guards as they changed in two-hour reliefs.
10062-8{_}3570{_}With his facts well collected he visited Mrs. Lanview, and at last he was confronted by Butler's agent.
10062-8{_}3571{_}This agent was a middle-aged man, who had evidently once been very handsome, but dissipation had left pitiable traces upon his fine features, and his once large, open eyes, that perplexingly suggested some one Barney tried in vain to recall--vainly?
10062-8{_}3572{_}The man didn't say much in the lady's presence, but when the two were in the open air, facing toward the center of the town, he divulged a good deal that surprised Barney.
10062-8{_}3573{_}"You are from Acredale, young man.
10062-8{_}3574{_}I lived there when I was younger than I am now.
10062-8{_}3575{_}My name?
10062-8{_}3576{_}People call me a good many names.
10062-8{_}3577{_}I don't mind at all, so that I have rum enough and a bed and a bite to eat.
10062-8{_}3578{_}No man can have more than that, my boy.
10062-8{_}3579{_}I am plain Dick Jones now.
10062-8{_}3580{_}It's an easy name, and plenty of the same in the land; and if I should die suddenly there would be lots o' folks to feel sorry, eh?
10062-8{_}3581{_}But as you are from Acredale I don't mind telling you that it is Elisha Boone that foots the bill.
10062-8{_}3582{_}Butler is a friend of Boone's, and he has given me authority to summon all the troops within reach to my aid.
10062-8{_}3583{_}My business is to carry young Wes Boone to Fort Monroe.
10062-8{_}3584{_}Butler doesn't know that.
10062-8{_}3585{_}He thinks I am spying Jeff Davis and piping for the prisoners.
10062-8{_}3586{_}He didn't say that he wanted me to kill Davis, but if we could carry him to Fort Monroe, my boy, there'd be about a million dollars swag to divide!
10062-8{_}3587{_}How does that strike you?"
10062-8{_}3588{_}"It doesn't strike me at all.
10062-8{_}3589{_}I think it is for the interest of the Union that Davis should be where he is.
10062-8{_}3590{_}He is vain, arrogant, silly, and dull.
10062-8{_}3591{_}He will alone wreck the rebel cause if he is given time.
10062-8{_}3592{_}There couldn't be a greater misfortune for the North than to have Davis displaced by some one of real ability, such as Stephens, Lee, Benjamin, Mason, Breckenridge, or, in fact, any of the men identified with secession."
10062-8{_}3593{_}"You surprise me, my son.
10062-8{_}3594{_}Still, admitting all you say, the men who should surprise the North some fine morning with a present of Jeff Davis on their breakfast-plates, wouldn't be without honor, to say nothing of promotion and profit"  "Oh, if we can carry Jeff off without compromising the safety of the prisoners, I'll join you heartily.
10062-8{_}3595{_}But first of all we must rescue them."
10062-8{_}3596{_}"Unquestionably; now, here's the programme: Butler's forces will be within gunshot of Magruder's lines on Warwick Creek Thursday--that's three days from now.
10062-8{_}3597{_}The prisoners will be out of the sewer Wednesday after midnight.
10062-8{_}3598{_}You know the roads eastward.
10062-8{_}3599{_}You will lead them to the swamps near Williamsburg.
10062-8{_}3600{_}There we will have boats to take part down the river; the rest will make through the swamps under my lead.
10062-8{_}3601{_}I have been spying out the land for a week.
10062-8{_}3602{_}At a place called Rosedale we pick up young Boone, who is really the object of my journey.
10062-8{_}3603{_}I couldn't find him for weeks, and inquired of all the prisoners.
10062-8{_}3604{_}Mrs. Lanview finally put me on the track, and I saw Wes Boone as I came up here.
10062-8{_}3605{_}He thought the chances were better with a big party than alone.
10062-8{_}3606{_}I saw him again yesterday, and he told me that Davis and Lee, his chief of staff, were to be at a party in the Rosedale house on Thursday next.
10062-8{_}3607{_}Now, we can pick up Davis just as well as Boone.
10062-8{_}3608{_}There is the whole plan."
10062-8{_}3609{_}"Oh, that's a different matter.
10062-8{_}3610{_}Davis will not be near the city, and his keeping will not add to our danger.
10062-8{_}3611{_}I see no reason why we shouldn't grab him.
10062-8{_}3612{_}Heavens, what a sensation it will make!
10062-8{_}3613{_}We shall be the wonder of the North--we shall he like the men that discovered André and Arnold--Paulding and--and"--but here Barney's historical facts came to an end--"we shall be famous for--forever!"
10062-8{_}3614{_}"For a week, my son; wonders don't live long in these fast days.
10062-8{_}3615{_}For a week the North will glorify us; then, if they find that we voted for Douglas, as I did, they will say we had some sinister design in bringing Davis North, and likely send us to Fort Lafayette."
10062-8{_}3616{_}Barney stopped dead; they had come under a gas-lamp between Grace and Franklin Streets.
10062-8{_}3617{_}He looked at the man.
10062-8{_}3618{_}He was quite sober.
10062-8{_}3619{_}His eyes answered the young man's indignant protesting glance, openly, unshrinkingly, humorously.
10062-8{_}3620{_}"I should be sorry to think that, Mr.
10062-8{_}3621{_}Jones."
10062-8{_}3622{_}"Well, wait.
10062-8{_}3623{_}When you get North you will see a mighty change in things.
10062-8{_}3624{_}Sentiment, my boy, follows the main chance.
10062-8{_}3625{_}It's money, my boy, money.
10062-8{_}3626{_}Enough money would have made Judas respectable; he was fool enough to put his price too low."
10062-8{_}3627{_}"Ugh!--you almost make me hate the North!
10062-8{_}3628{_}Who can have heart to fight for such heartless traffickers?"
10062-8{_}3629{_}"The North doesn't ask your heart.
10062-8{_}3630{_}It has counted the cost, and finds that it can pay a million of men thirteen dollars a month for three years, and still make a good thing out of it--that's about the breadth of it.
10062-8{_}3631{_}Here's an oasis in the desert of darkness.
10062-8{_}3632{_}Come and have a drink?"
10062-8{_}3633{_}But Barney--not caring for a drink, the cynic--gave him his address, and, dreadfully cast down in spirit, the eager partisan moped up the long hill homeward.
10062-8{_}3634{_}The next day Mrs. Lanview gave him the details of the meditated escape.
10062-8{_}3635{_}There were only sixty or a hundred in position to avail themselves of the subterranean way that had been toilsomely dug, by a few devoted spirits, with tools casually dropped among them by the guileless Veronica during her daily visits.
10062-8{_}3636{_}The plotters counted on at least six hours' start before discovery.
10062-8{_}3637{_}The guards were not to be disturbed, and the evasion would not be known until eight o'clock, when the miserable breakfast ration was distributed.
10062-8{_}3638{_}Of that amazing-exploit, the digging through twenty solid feet of earth and stone, I do not propose to tell.
10062-8{_}3639{_}It is to be found in the journals of the day: it is contained in the hundred pathetic narratives of the men who took part.
10062-8{_}3640{_}It has nothing to do with this history beyond the use made of it to mislead the ingenious Barney, and in the end complicate the careers of those in whom we are interested.
10062-8{_}3641{_}Suffice it, therefore, to say that in the dim morning mist, as arranged, a shadowy host emerged on the river-bottom, now dry and footable; that each man, as he crawled from the pit, was directed into the thick willows bordering the banks; that when six score or more had clambered out they obeyed a whispered command, for which Veronica had prepared them, and noiselessly, in shadowy single file, they followed the bed of the stream, even where the water flowed deep and dangerous, until they came to the gentle slopes of Church Hill.
10062-8{_}3642{_}Then, under guidance of Barney, those who were wise followed swiftly down the river-road until daylight, when they hid in the dim recesses of the white-oak swamps, where they lay concealed many hours.
10062-8{_}3643{_}As night fell they faced hopefully forward down the Williamsburg road, until a flaming wave in the air admonished them to strike to the right, and they plunged into the pathless swamps of the Chickahominy.
10062-8{_}3644{_}Here they were secure.
10062-8{_}3645{_}No force able to cope with them could enter; no force at the command of Magruder could surround them.
10062-8{_}3646{_}But Barney's guiding hand was now replaced by another.
10062-8{_}3647{_}Jones had appeared, and with him men bearing Butler's commission.
10062-8{_}3648{_}The prisoners of Libby set up a defiant cheer.
10062-8{_}3649{_}They were once more under the flag.
10062-8{_}3650{_}Father Abraham was again their commander.
10062-8{_}3651{_}There were sedate, fatherly men among these rescued bands.
10062-8{_}3652{_}There were men with gray hairs and sober behavior; men who could bow meekly under the chastening rod; but the antics of the juvenile group, in which we are mainly interested, were grave and decorous compared with the abandoned, delirious joy of these grave men as they reached the recesses of a swamp that denied admission to all save practiced explorers.
10062-8{_}3653{_}Why, here they could subsist for weeks!
10062-8{_}3654{_}The rebels might spy them, might surround them, but they need not starve--the buds were food, the bushes refreshment, the pellucid pools drink and life.
10062-8{_}3655{_}Barney stared in speechless amazement at the unseemly gambols of the motley mass.
10062-8{_}3656{_}Delirium!
10062-8{_}3657{_}it was a mild term for the embracing, the prancing, the Carmagnole-like ecstasy of the half-clad madmen running amuck in the almost unendurable joy of liberation.
10062-8{_}3658{_}Barney knew that this condition of things would never do.
10062-8{_}3659{_}All who bore commissions in the army were selected from the men.
10062-8{_}3660{_}The highest in rank, who proved to be a colonel, was invested with the command, Barney serving as adjutant, and Jones as guide.
10062-8{_}3661{_}The rabble, having made a good meal from the spoil of a sweet-potato patch, pushed forward through the fretwork of fern, rank morass, and verdure, toward security.
10062-8{_}3662{_}But the march was a snail's pace, as may be imagined.
10062-8{_}3663{_}The men, worn to skeletons by months of captivity, insufficient food, and stinted exercise, were forced to halt often for rest in such toilsome marching as the half-aquatic surface of the swamp involved.
10062-8{_}3664{_}By Thursday noon they were still far from the river.
10062-8{_}3665{_}Foragers were detailed to procure food, and pending their return the wearied band sank to the earth to rest.
10062-8{_}3666{_}In less than two hours the predatory platoon returned with a sybaritic store--chickens, young lamb, green corn, onions.
10062-8{_}3667{_}Only the stern command of the colonel suppressed a mighty cheer.
10062-8{_}3668{_}When the march was resumed the colonel led the main column south by east.
10062-8{_}3669{_}Jones, with Barney and a dozen men, struck due east.
10062-8{_}3670{_}In answer to Barney's surprised question, Jones informed him they were to pick up "Wes" Boone by taking that route.
10062-8{_}3671{_}Difficult as the way had been heretofore, it now became laborious in the extreme for this smaller band.
10062-8{_}3672{_}The bottom was all under water, and before they had proceeded a mile half the group were drenched.
10062-8{_}3673{_}In many cases an imprudent plunger was compelled to call a halt to rescue his shoes--that is, those who were lucky enough to have shoes--from the deep mud, hidden by a fair green surface of moss or tendrils.
10062-8{_}3674{_}It was a wondrous journey to Barney, The pages of Sindbad alone seemed to have a parallel for the awful mysteries of that long, long flight through jungles of towering timber, whose leaves and bark were as unfamiliar as Brazilian growth to the troops of Pizarro or the Congo vegetation to the French pioneer.
10062-8{_}3675{_}Jones and his comrades saw nothing but the hardships of the march and the delay of the painful _détours_ in the solemn glades.
10062-8{_}3676{_}The direction was kept by compass, many of the men having been supplied with a miniature instrument by the prudent foresight of Mrs. Lanview, who was niggard of neither time nor money in the cause she had at heart.
10062-8{_}3677{_}In spite of every effort a march so swift that it would have exhausted cavalry, Jones's ranks did not reach the rendezvous until midnight.
10062-8{_}3678{_}At about that hour the exhausted fugitives came suddenly upon a wide, open plain, and far below them, in the valley, a vision of light and life shone through the dark.
10062-8{_}3679{_}"There, boys, we're at the end of our first stage.
10062-8{_}3680{_}Unless I'm much mistaken, that bit of merry-making yonder will cost the Confederacy a chief."
10062-8{_}3681{_}"But is it certain that Davis is there?"
10062-8{_}3682{_}asked the man Jones called Moon, who seemed to be his intimate.
10062-8{_}3683{_}"Ah, that we will learn so soon as Nasmyd reports.
10062-8{_}3684{_}We will give the signal when we reach that fringe of wood yonder.
10062-8{_}3685{_}It's back of the grounds, separated from them by a hard piece of swamp and water.--Men, you must follow now in single file, and when we get in the swamp, mind, a single step out of line will cost you your lives, for, sucked into that morass, wild horses can't pull you out."
10062-8{_}3686{_}Then, as they plunged anew in the gloomy deeps of swamp and brake, the friendly lights were lost and the depressed wayfarers struggled on with something of the feeling of a crew cast away at sea, who, thrown upon the crest of a rising billow, catch a near glimpse of a great ship, light and taut, riding serenely havenward to lose it the next in the dire waste.
10062-8{_}3687{_}Presently the melancholy bird-notes that had puzzled Jack in the same vicinity days before broke out just in front of Barney, who was clambering along, the third man from the head of the little column.
10062-8{_}3688{_}Again, after a long pause, the sweet, plaintive note was re-echoed from a distance.
10062-8{_}3689{_}"Ah, all is well!"
10062-8{_}3690{_}he heard Jones ejaculate triumphantly.
10062-8{_}3691{_}"We are in time and we are waited for.--Now, men, put all the heart that's in you to the next half-hour's work.
10062-8{_}3692{_}No danger, but just cool heads and strong arms."
10062-8{_}3693{_}This good news was conveyed from man to man, and the toilsome movement briskly accelerated under the inspiring watchword.
10062-8{_}3694{_}Shortly afterward the larger growth--cypress and oak--diminished, as the band straggled into the open, starry night at the margin of what they could tell was water by the croaking of frogs and plashing of night birds and reptiles.
10062-8{_}3695{_}Then the train was halted.
10062-8{_}3696{_}Jones left Nasmyd in command and plunged into a thick skirt of bushes.
10062-8{_}3697{_}Now Barney, hot and dirty from the march, had shot ahead when he heard the ripple of the water.
10062-8{_}3698{_}He had taken off his shoes to bathe his blistered and swollen feet, and sat quite still and restful under the leafy sprays of an odorous bush that even in the dark he knew to be honeysuckle.
10062-8{_}3699{_}"Well," he heard Jones cry in an exultant whisper, "we've done it.
10062-8{_}3700{_}The woman is a trump.
10062-8{_}3701{_}There are a hundred nearly of the prisoners gone to the boats.
10062-8{_}3702{_}Now we are ready for Boone.
10062-8{_}3703{_}Is Davis here?"
10062-8{_}3704{_}"Yes; he came over from Williamsburg at eight o'clock; they were feasting when Clem came away a three or more ago."
10062-8{_}3705{_}"Any cavalry at the house?"
10062-8{_}3706{_}"A squadron; but they are ordered to be in saddle for their quarters at midnight.
10062-8{_}3707{_}There's the bugle for boots and saddles now."
10062-8{_}3708{_}"Yes; by the Eternal, what luck!
10062-8{_}3709{_}Davis will sleep there."
10062-8{_}3710{_}"So Clem says; the state chamber has been prepared for him; all the rest except Lee go back to Williamsburg."
10062-8{_}3711{_}"We couldn't have arranged it better if we had been given the ordering of it.
10062-8{_}3712{_}Are all the boats here?"
10062-8{_}3713{_}"Yes."
10062-8{_}3714{_}"And the negroes--how many have you?"
10062-8{_}3715{_}"I can't say.
10062-8{_}3716{_}They've been dropping across in twos and threes since ten o'clock.
10062-8{_}3717{_}The curious thing is that the women are more taken with the idea of fight than the men.
10062-8{_}3718{_}We shall have enough--too many, I fear."
10062-8{_}3719{_}"We'll make them our safety, Jim, my boy; we'll divide them up, and, in case of pursuit, send them in different directions to confuse the troops."
10062-8{_}3720{_}"How many men are you going to take to the house?"
10062-8{_}3721{_}"Six, with you and me.
10062-8{_}3722{_}It will be unsafe to take more, as the boats are small.
10062-8{_}3723{_}I will go back and select the men.
10062-8{_}3724{_}You get the boats ready."
10062-8{_}3725{_}Barney hurried on his shoes, crawled through the bushes, and was in his place when Jones presently appeared.
10062-8{_}3726{_}The men, dead tired, were disposed about on the ground asleep, not minding the damp grass or the heavy dew that made the air fairly misty.
10062-8{_}3727{_}"Wake four of the men," Jones whispered, and when they were aroused he said to a tall, reeling shadow, idly waiting orders:  "We'll be back in a half-hour, or an hour at the farthest.
10062-8{_}3728{_}Let the men sleep; they need it.
10062-8{_}3729{_}Sleep yourself if you want to.
10062-8{_}3730{_}Moon or I will come to rouse you, and we will bring you plenty of bacon and hominy.
10062-8{_}3731{_}Have no fears if you hear movements just beyond you; there are a couple of contrabands here who go with us.
10062-8{_}3732{_}Here's a ration of tobacco for the men when they wake, and a gallon of whisky, which you must serve out gradually."
10062-8{_}3733{_}Revived by this stimulating news quite as much as by the whisky, Barney and his three comrades followed Jones to the boats.
10062-8{_}3734{_}There were four--the dug-outs we saw Jack manoeuvring in the same waters a few nights before.
10062-8{_}3735{_}A negro sat silent, shadowy in each, and, when Jones gave the word, "Let drive!"
10062-8{_}3736{_}the barks shot through the waters, propelled by the single scull, as swiftly as an Indian canoe.
10062-8{_}3737{_}In a few moments all debarked on the grassy knoll behind the black line of hedge.
10062-8{_}3738{_}Jones made straight for the high doorway, and inserting a key it was noiselessly opened.
10062-8{_}3739{_}"Men," he whispered, "no names must be used in any case.
10062-8{_}3740{_}I'm number one, Jim here is number two, Moore number three, and so on.
10062-8{_}3741{_}Each one remember his number.
10062-8{_}3742{_}Clem will remain here with number six to guard the gate.
10062-8{_}3743{_}All the rest follow me."
10062-8{_}3744{_}Two negroes joined the party that stole forward through the rose-field to the negro quarters.
10062-8{_}3745{_}All was silent.
10062-8{_}3746{_}As they reached the great kitchen behind the house and connected with it by a trellised pavilion, only an occasional light could be seen in the house.
10062-8{_}3747{_}All were apparently there.
10062-8{_}3748{_}The ball had ended.
10062-8{_}3749{_}Leaving Barney in charge of the rest, Jones and Number Two crept along the trellis toward the house and soon disappeared around the southern corner.
10062-8{_}3750{_}Jones presently returned and said, exultingly:  "The cavalry is gone; we have nothing to fear.--Plato, you go with Number Two to the stables and bring the horses out; hold six and send the rest scattering in the fields, so that in case of anybody's being in the mind to follow hell have to use his legs, and we can beat them at that game.
10062-8{_}3751{_}Where are the ropes?"
10062-8{_}3752{_}he asked the black man left in the group.
10062-8{_}3753{_}"In de kitchen, massa."
10062-8{_}3754{_}"Get them!"
10062-8{_}3755{_}"Must I go alone, massa?"
10062-8{_}3756{_}"That's a fact.--There, Moore, you go with the boy--don't be a minute."
10062-8{_}3757{_}Barney followed the sable marauder through the grounds to the rear of the trellis, and crept with him through a window which stood open.
10062-8{_}3758{_}The kitchen was dark, but the negro seemed perfectly familiar with the place.
10062-8{_}3759{_}He made directly for a dark panel in the northern wall, opened a cupboard-door, knelt down and began to grope among bottles, boxes, and what not that housewives gather in such receptacles.
10062-8{_}3760{_}"Oh, de lor'!
10062-8{_}3761{_}dey ain't no rope!
10062-8{_}3762{_}It's done gone!"
10062-8{_}3763{_}"Have you a match?"
10062-8{_}3764{_}Barney asked.
10062-8{_}3765{_}"No, massa, but dey is some yondah."
10062-8{_}3766{_}"Find them."
10062-8{_}3767{_}The boy crept cautiously in the direction of the passage leading into the house; he fumbled about, an age, as it seemed to the impatient Barney, and at last uttered an exclamation:  "Got 'em?"
10062-8{_}3768{_}"No, massa, but Ise suah deys kep dar."
10062-8{_}3769{_}"Take my hand and lead me."
10062-8{_}3770{_}"It's molasses, massa, and Ise all stickem," the voice in the dark whispered, delightedly, and Barney could see a double row of glistening white ivory in the dim light that came through the window.
10062-8{_}3771{_}He came nearer the clumsy wight, and saw that it was a pan of batter the cook had left on the table, probably the morning griddle-cakes.
10062-8{_}3772{_}The negro was a mass of white, pasty glue, and knelt on the floor, licking his hands passively.
10062-8{_}3773{_}"Where are the matches?"
10062-8{_}3774{_}"Under de clock, in a tin safe, massa--right da."
10062-8{_}3775{_}Barney groped angrily about the table, on the clock-shelf, knocking down a tin dish, that fell with the clatter of a bursting magazine in the dense stillness of the night.
10062-8{_}3776{_}Both drew back in shadow, waiting with heart-beats that sounded in their ears like tramping horses on thick sward.
10062-8{_}3777{_}The clamor of rushing steeds in the lane suddenly drowned this; a loud, joyous whinny sounded in the very kitchen it seemed, and there was a rush houseward past the pantry as of a troop of cavalry.
10062-8{_}3778{_}Then a blood-curdling outcry of voices, then shots.
10062-8{_}3779{_}Barney, leaving the negro writhing in convulsions under the table, darted to the window--to the rendezvous.
10062-8{_}3780{_}It was deserted.
10062-8{_}3781{_}CHAPTER XIX.
10062-8{_}3782{_}"HE EITHER FEARS HIS FATE TOO MUCH."
10062-8{_}3783{_}When Vincent visited the stables on the morning of that eagerly-looked-for Thursday, he found three of the horses clammy with perspiration and giving every sign of having been ridden!
10062-8{_}3784{_}The awkward and evasive answers of the stablemen would not have been enough for any other than a man preoccupied by love.
10062-8{_}3785{_}When Rosa went to the kitchen, if her head had not been taken up with the love in her heart, she must certainly have remarked that the stores of food prepared for the household were curiously diminished and the kitchen girls unwontedly reserved.
10062-8{_}3786{_}Indeed, in any other condition than that in which the family now found themselves, they must have remarked a singular change in the black brigade in kitchen and garden.
10062-8{_}3787{_}But, preocupied each with a different interest, as well as the preparation for the President's _fête_, the Atterburys remarked nothing sinister in the distracted conduct of their servants, and had only a vague feeling that the great event had in some sort paralyzed their wonted noisy activities and repressed their usual chatter.
10062-8{_}3788{_}Kate's uneasiness and restless vagaries, her disjointed talk and half-guilty evasions, would have been remarked by her prepossessed hosts; while Wesley's shifting and moody silence would have warned his comrades that he was suffering the pangs of an evil done or meditated.
10062-8{_}3789{_}Precursive signs like these--and much more, which need not be dwelt on--the kind hosts of Rosedale made no note of.
10062-8{_}3790{_}But when Vincent opened the mail-bag--brought by an orderly from Williamsburg every morning, the first surprise and shock of the day was felt--though in varying degrees by all the diverse inmates of the house.
10062-8{_}3791{_}"Hah!
10062-8{_}3792{_}glory to the Lord of hosts!"
10062-8{_}3793{_}the exultant reader cried, as he passed to his mother a large official envelope at the breakfast-table.
10062-8{_}3794{_}"I'm ordered to the field."
10062-8{_}3795{_}he cried, as Jack looked inquiringly; "I'm to set out to-night and report for duty with General Johnston to-morrow at Manassas.
10062-8{_}3796{_}No more loitering in my lady's bower; Jack, my boy, the carpet will be clear for your knightly pranks after to-night."
10062-8{_}3797{_}"If it were Aladdin's magic rug, I should caper nimbly enough.
10062-8{_}3798{_}I warrant you."
10062-8{_}3799{_}"What would you wish--if it were under your feet, with its slaves at your command?"
10062-8{_}3800{_}"I should whisk you all off--North--instanter."
10062-8{_}3801{_}"Ingrate!--plunge us into the chilly blasts of the North, in return for our glorious Southern sun?
10062-8{_}3802{_}Fie, Jack!
10062-8{_}3803{_}I'm surprised at such selfish ingratitude.
10062-8{_}3804{_}We expected better things of our prisoners," Mrs. Atterbury murmured, and affected a reproving frown at the culprit, as she handed her son back the order, with a stilled sigh.
10062-8{_}3805{_}"The sun of the South is not the sun of York to us, you know; all the clouds that lower on our house are doubly darkened by this Southern sun; even the warmth of Rosedale hearts can not make up for our eclipsed Northern star," Jack said, sadly, with a wistful look at the rival warrior reading with sparkling eyes the instructions accompanying the order to march.
10062-8{_}3806{_}"Since Vincent is going so far northward, I think it will be a good time for us to go home," Mrs. Sprague began, tentatively.
10062-8{_}3807{_}"Oh--no--no!
10062-8{_}3808{_}Oh, we could never think of such a thing," Rosa cried--"could we, mamma?"
10062-8{_}3809{_}"Why should you go?"
10062-8{_}3810{_}Mrs. Atterbury asked.
10062-8{_}3811{_}"Until Jack is exchanged, you've certainly no duty in the North so important as watching over this headstrong fellow.
10062-8{_}3812{_}We can't think of your going--unless you are weary of us."
10062-8{_}3813{_}"O Mrs. Atterbury, pray don't put it in that way!
10062-8{_}3814{_}You know better.
10062-8{_}3815{_}Our visit here has been perfect.
10062-8{_}3816{_}But you can understand my anxiety to be at home; to be where I can aid my son's release.
10062-8{_}3817{_}I have been anxious for some time to broach the subject, but I saw that our going would be a trouble to you; now, since fortune offers this chance, we must seize it--that is, those of us who feel it a duty to go"; and she looked meaningly at Merry and her daughter.
10062-8{_}3818{_}"Nonsense!
10062-8{_}3819{_}You are hostages for Vincent, in case he is captured, as long as you are here; I can't let you go--under the laws of war--I can not.
10062-8{_}3820{_}Can I, Vincent?"
10062-8{_}3821{_}Vincent looked at Jack solemnly, but made no answer.
10062-8{_}3822{_}"Mamma is quite right.
10062-8{_}3823{_}While you are with us no harm can come to Vincent; for, if he should be taken prisoner, we can threaten the Yankee Government to put you to torture unless he is well treated," Rosa interrupted, reassuringly.
10062-8{_}3824{_}"We should be far more aid and comfort to Vincent if we were in the North than we could be here.
10062-8{_}3825{_}If he were taken prisoner and wounded, we could return him the kindness we have received here.
10062-8{_}3826{_}In any event, we could lessen the hardships of prison life."
10062-8{_}3827{_}"Oh, you would have to minister to a mind diseased, if such a fate should befall me!"
10062-8{_}3828{_}Vincent cried, sentimentally; with a glance into Olympia's eyes, which met his at the moment.
10062-8{_}3829{_}Both blushed; and Olympia, to relieve the embarrassment, said, decisively:  "Mamma is right.
10062-8{_}3830{_}Jack must have his family on the ground, to watch over his interests.
10062-8{_}3831{_}I am sure there is some underhand work responsible for this long delay in his case, for I saw by _The Whig_, last week, that exchanges of prisoners had been made; I think that--" But, suddenly remembering the presence of Kate and Wesley, she did not finish the thought, which implied a belief in the intervention of the elder Boone--to Jack's detriment.
10062-8{_}3832{_}In the end--when the two mothers talked the matter over--Mrs. Sprague carried the point.
10062-8{_}3833{_}She convinced Mrs. Atterbury that there was danger to Jack in a longer stay of his family in the Confederate lines.
10062-8{_}3834{_}Vague reports had already reached them from Acredale of the suspicious hostility in which the Democrats were held after Bull Run.
10062-8{_}3835{_}The Northern papers, which came through the lines quite regularly, left no doubt that Democratic leanings were universally interpreted in the North as evidences of rebel sympathy, if not partisanship.
10062-8{_}3836{_}Such a charge, as things stood, would be fatal to Jack; and the mother's duty was plain.
10062-8{_}3837{_}She had friends in Washington, once powerful, who could stand between her son and calumny--perhaps more serious danger--when she was present in person to explain his conduct.
10062-8{_}3838{_}If she could not at once secure his exchange, she could save him from compromise in the present inflammable and capricious state of the public mind.
10062-8{_}3839{_}Understanding this, and the enmity of Boone, Mrs. Atterbury not only made no further objection, but acknowledged the urgent necessity of the mother's presence in the North.
10062-8{_}3840{_}The idle life of Rosedale had grown unbearably irksome to Merry, too.
10062-8{_}3841{_}"I feel as if I were a rebel," she confided to Mrs. Sprague in the evening talks, when the piano sounded and the young people were making the hours pass in gayety.
10062-8{_}3842{_}"It's a sin for us to laugh and be contented here, when our friends are bearing the burdens of war.
10062-8{_}3843{_}I shall be ashamed to show my face in Acredale.
10062-8{_}3844{_}Oh, I wish I could carry a musket!"
10062-8{_}3845{_}"You might carry a canteen, my dear.
10062-8{_}3846{_}I believe the regiments take out _vivandières_--there would be an outlet for your warlike emotions," Mrs. Sprague said, with the purpose of cheering the unhappy spinster.
10062-8{_}3847{_}"Ah, no; I must not give encouragement to that dreadful Richard.
10062-8{_}3848{_}But we shall go now, thank Heaven, and it will comfort my sisters to have the boy back on Northern soil, even if he persists in being a soldier."
10062-8{_}3849{_}She had a long talk with Jack on the subject.
10062-8{_}3850{_}That tempest-tossed knight convinced her that it would only incite the boy to more unruliness to persist in his quitting the army, or to urge him northward now, before an exchange was properly arranged.
10062-8{_}3851{_}Indeed, he was a prisoner--taken in battle--though his name did not appear on the lists.
10062-8{_}3852{_}So Vincent's sudden going was welcomed as a stroke of good fortune.
10062-8{_}3853{_}The Atterburys, understanding the natural feelings of the family, made only perfunctory opposition.
10062-8{_}3854{_}Olympia and Kate were to remain until their brothers' fates were decided.
10062-8{_}3855{_}Vincent, who had been for weeks wildly impatient to return to the field, was divided in mind now--by joy and despair.
10062-8{_}3856{_}He had put off and put off a last appeal to Olympia.
10062-8{_}3857{_}He had not had an opportunity, or rather had too much opportunity--and had, from day to day, deferred the longed-for yet dreaded decision.
10062-8{_}3858{_}When ready to speak, prudence whispered that it would be better to leave the question open until it should come up of itself.
10062-8{_}3859{_}She would learn every day to know him better in his own home, where all the artificialities of life are stripped from a man, by the concurrent abrasions of family love and domestic _devoirs_.
10062-8{_}3860{_}She would see that, however unworthy of her love he might have seemed in the old boyish days at Acredale, now he could be a man when manliness was demanded; that he could be patient, reticent, humble in the trials her caprice or coquetry put upon him.
10062-8{_}3861{_}She had, it seemed to him, deepened and broadened the current of his love during these blissful weeks of waiting.
10062-8{_}3862{_}Her very reserve, under the new conditions surrounding her, had made more luminous the beauty of her heart and mind.
10062-8{_}3863{_}She was no longer the airy, capricious Olympia of his college days.
10062-8{_}3864{_}The pensive gravity of misfortune and premature responsibility had ennobled and made more tangible the traits that had won him in her Northern home.
10062-8{_}3865{_}She had not avoided him during these weeks of purifying probation, as he feared she would.
10062-8{_}3866{_}Of late--Jack's state being secure--she had revived much of the old vivacity, and deepened the thrall that held him.
10062-8{_}3867{_}But now the merry-making season which had opened before them was at an end.
10062-8{_}3868{_}The madrigals that welled up in his soft heart must sing themselves in the silence of the night, in the camp yonder, with no ears to comprehend, no heart to melt to them.
10062-8{_}3869{_}He should probably not get a chance to see her again during the conflict.
10062-8{_}3870{_}How long?
10062-8{_}3871{_}Perhaps a year--for it would take two campaigns, as the rebel leaders reckoned, to convince the North that the Confederacy was unconquerable!
10062-8{_}3872{_}And what might not happen during those momentous months?
10062-8{_}3873{_}Perhaps Jack's death?--and then they would be divided as by fire--or, if the conflict resulted victoriously for the South, as he knew it must, he foresaw that the soldier of the conquering army would not be received as a wooer in the family of the defeated.
10062-8{_}3874{_}He knew her so well!
10062-8{_}3875{_}She would, in the very pride of outraged patriotism, give her love to one of the defeated, rather than add to the triumphs of the hated South.
10062-8{_}3876{_}She had strong convictions on the war.
10062-8{_}3877{_}She hated slavery, and she could not be made to see that the South was warring for liberty, not to sustain slavery.
10062-8{_}3878{_}These thoughts ran through Vincent's troubled mind as his mother directed the preparations for the _fête_ of the President.
10062-8{_}3879{_}Kate, Jack, and Dick were pressed into the service of decorating the apartments.
10062-8{_}3880{_}Olympia left the room with her mother to advise and assist in making ready for the journey North; and Vincent, aiding his mother with a sadly divided mind, kept furtive watch on the hallway.
10062-8{_}3881{_}She held him hours in suspense, he thought, almost wrathfully, of deliberate purpose; for she must have read in his eyes that he wanted to talk with her.
10062-8{_}3882{_}The artless Dick finally gave him a chance.
10062-8{_}3883{_}"I say, Vint, get Polly to show you the roses needed for the tables; I'll be with you by-and-by to cut the ferns.
10062-8{_}3884{_}Do you think you could make yourself of that much use?
10062-8{_}3885{_}You're not worth a straw here"  "Send for Miss Polly and I'll do my best," Vincent said, with a gulp, to conceal his joy.
10062-8{_}3886{_}She appeared presently; and, as they were passing out of the door, Rosa cried, imperiously:  "Oh, yes, Vint, we need ever so much honeysuckle; you know where it hangs thickest--in the Owl's Glen.
10062-8{_}3887{_}Olympia will like to see that--the haunt of her favorite bird"; and the busy little maid laughed cheerily, like a disordered goddess, intoxicated by the exhaling odors of the floral chaos.
10062-8{_}3888{_}"_En route_ for Roumelia, then," Vincent cried in military cadence, as the florists set out.
10062-8{_}3889{_}Roumelia was the name Jack had given the rose-lands near the stream, in fanciful allusion to the Turkish province of flowers.
10062-8{_}3890{_}Halting at the gardener's cottage, Vincent procured an immense pair of shears, like a double rapier in size, and, bidding the man follow to gather the blossoms, he pushed into the blooming vineyard.
10062-8{_}3891{_}"With such an instrument I should say it was the golden fleece you were after," Olympia cried, as he reached her side, "though I believe Jason didn't do the shearing."
10062-8{_}3892{_}"No, the powers of air worked for him, and he found his quest ready to his hand."
10062-8{_}3893{_}"I'm sure the powers of air have not denied you; look at those radiant ranks of blossoms bending to be gathered."
10062-8{_}3894{_}"Ah, yes, beauty stoops sometimes to welcome the trembling hand of the suitor."
10062-8{_}3895{_}"Your hand is rather unsteady--infirm of purpose; give me the blades."
10062-8{_}3896{_}She took them laughingly, and snipped the green stems rapidly and dexterously.
10062-8{_}3897{_}"Yes, I believe men are infirm in moral purposes, as compared to women.
10062-8{_}3898{_}It is only in the brutalities of life that men are decisive."
10062-8{_}3899{_}"Do you mean that women approach the trials of life less thinkingly and act less rationally than men?"
10062-8{_}3900{_}"Yes and no.
10062-8{_}3901{_}The daring too much is always before a man; the daring too little is, I think, the only trouble a woman has."
10062-8{_}3902{_}"Oh, that is a large question, involving too much mental strain in a garden of roses, where the senses sleep and one is content with mere breath and the faintest motion."
10062-8{_}3903{_}"There are enough roses; now we will go for the wild smilax and honeysuckle; perhaps the cool air of the pools will restore your mental activities."
10062-8{_}3904{_}They left the dismembered roses scattered in fragrant heaps on the shaded path and walked slowly toward the dense hedge.
10062-8{_}3905{_}"What a perfect fortress this green wall makes of the gardens!"
10062-8{_}3906{_}Olympia said, glancing around the great square, where the solid green wall could be seen running up much higher than their heads.
10062-8{_}3907{_}"Yes, as I said the other day, it would take hard work for an invading force to get at the house unless traitors within gave up the gates.
10062-8{_}3908{_}This one," he added, unlocking a massive oak door, crossed with thick planks and studded with iron bolts, "alone admits from the creek and swamp.
10062-8{_}3909{_}It is locked all the time; no one has the key except the gardener, who delivers it to mamma every night."
10062-8{_}3910{_}"A feudal demesne; it takes one back to the so-called days of chivalry."
10062-8{_}3911{_}"Why do you say 'so-called'?
10062-8{_}3912{_}To me they are the delight of the past--when men went to battle for the smile of the women they loved, when knights rode the world over in search of adventure, and my lady, in her donjon, listened with pleasure to the lover's roundelay.
10062-8{_}3913{_}Ah, it was a perfect life, an enchanting time.
10062-8{_}3914{_}We are living in a coarse, brutal age; chivalry was the creed of civilization, the knights the priesthood of the higher life."
10062-8{_}3915{_}"There's the Southerner through and through in that sentimentality.
10062-8{_}3916{_}To me chivalry means all that is narrow, cruel, and rapacious in man.
10062-8{_}3917{_}The philandering knights were sensual boobies, the simpering dames soulless wantons.
10062-8{_}3918{_}Life meant simply the rule of the strong, the slaughter of the weak.
10062-8{_}3919{_}Servitude was its law and robbery its methods.
10062-8{_}3920{_}Have you ever traveled in out-of-the-way places in Germany, Austria, or Italy?"
10062-8{_}3921{_}"No, I've never been abroad."
10062-8{_}3922{_}"You would know better what I mean if you had seen the monstrous relics of the age you admire.
10062-8{_}3923{_}The few ruled the many; the knights were simply a brotherhood of blood and rapine; men were slaves, women were worse.
10062-8{_}3924{_}The bravest were as unlettered as your body-servant, the most beautiful dames as termagant as Penelope the cook.
10062-8{_}3925{_}At the table men and women ate from a common dish, without forks or spoons.
10062-8{_}3926{_}Men guzzled gallons of unfermented wine.
10062-8{_}3927{_}A bath was unknown.
10062-8{_}3928{_}Cleanliness was as unpracticed as Islamism in New York.
10062-8{_}3929{_}Ugh!
10062-8{_}3930{_}anything but chivalry for me."
10062-8{_}3931{_}"But surely the great lords were not what you represent.
10062-8{_}3932{_}They were gentle born, gentle bred.
10062-8{_}3933{_}They could not be robbers; they lived from great estates."
10062-8{_}3934{_}"They were the 'Knights of St. Nicholas,' which, in the slang of the middle ages, meant what they call in the West road agents; indeed, plain highwaymen they were called in England in Bacon's day."
10062-8{_}3935{_}Vincent bent over discomfited, and held the little shallop until Olympia was seated, and then pushed off into the murky stream.
10062-8{_}3936{_}"Do you see those streamers of loveliness waving welcome to you, fair damsel--Nature knows its kind?"
10062-8{_}3937{_}"That's one word for me and one for yourself," she cried, seizing the dainty pink sprays that now trailed over her head and shoulders as the boat glided along the fringe of hushes supporting the clinging vines.
10062-8{_}3938{_}"Oh, no, Olympia; I can't speak even one word for myself.
10062-8{_}3939{_}I have been trembling to do it this six weeks, but your eye had none of the invitation these starry blossoms offer us.
10062-8{_}3940{_}I am going to say now, Olympia, what I have to say--for after to-day there will be no chance; what has been on my mind you have long known.
10062-8{_}3941{_}You know that I love you; how much I love you, how impossible it is to think of life without you, I dare not venture to say to you, for you distrust our Southern exaggeration.
10062-8{_}3942{_}But I do love you; ah, my God!
10062-8{_}3943{_}all the world else--my mother, my sister, my duty seem nothing compared to the one passionate hope in my breast.
10062-8{_}3944{_}Do you believe me, Olympia--do you doubt me?"
10062-8{_}3945{_}"Far from it, Vincent--dear Vincent--no--no--sit where you are and listen to me--" She was deeply moved, and the lover in his heart cursed the luckless veils of blossom that she apparently, without design, drew before her face.
10062-8{_}3946{_}"I do believe all you say; I knew it before you said it.
10062-8{_}3947{_}But you remember we went over this very same ground before.
10062-8{_}3948{_}Since then, it is true, you have been the means of saving us much misery; how much I hardly dare think of when I look back to that dreadful day, when mamma lay in the fever of coming disease and the hopelessness of despair.
10062-8{_}3949{_}All I can say, dear, dear Vincent, is what I said before.
10062-8{_}3950{_}Wait until thine and mine are no longer at war.
10062-8{_}3951{_}Wait until one flag covers us--"  "But that can never be!"
10062-8{_}3952{_}"Wait!
10062-8{_}3953{_}I have faith that it will be!"
10062-8{_}3954{_}"If one flag should cover us--my flag--would you--would you--?"
10062-8{_}3955{_}"Ah, Vincent!
10062-8{_}3956{_}don't ask me; don't force me to say something thing that will make you unhappy, since I don't know my own mind well enough yet to answer as you wish me to answer--"  "But you can tell me now whether you love me, or, at least, whether there is any one you love more?"
10062-8{_}3957{_}"I don't think I love you.
10062-8{_}3958{_}I know, however, that I think no more of any one else than I think of you; pray, let that suffice."
10062-8{_}3959{_}"But how cruel that is, Olympia!
10062-8{_}3960{_}It is as much, as to say that you won't wait and see whether you may meet some one that you can be surer of than you are of me?"
10062-8{_}3961{_}"I must distress you whatever I say, Vincent!
10062-8{_}3962{_}Frankly, I don't think you can decide just now whether your heart is really engaged.
10062-8{_}3963{_}I think you do not know me as a man should knows the woman he makes his wife.
10062-8{_}3964{_}I am certain I do not know you.
10062-8{_}3965{_}If you had been born and bred in the North, I should have no difficulty in deciding; but your ways are so different here: women are accorded so much before marriage, and made so little of a man's life after marriage, that I shrink from a promise which, if lightly or inconsiderately given, would bring the last misery a woman can confront."
10062-8{_}3966{_}"What, Olympia!
10062-8{_}3967{_}you think Southern men do not hold marriage to be sacred?"
10062-8{_}3968{_}"I think that the Southern man has a good deal of the knight you spoke of in him, and, like the Frenchman, marries inconsiderately, and does penance in infidelity, at least to the form, if not the fact, of the relation."
10062-8{_}3969{_}"O Olympia!
10062-8{_}3970{_}where do you get such repulsive ideas of us; who has been traducing us to you?"
10062-8{_}3971{_}"I judge from the Southern men I have seen North; pardon me, Vincent, I do not see how it can be otherwise in a society based upon human servitude.
10062-8{_}3972{_}To live on the labors of a helot people blunts the finer sensibilities of men and women alike; when you can look unshrinkingly at the separation of husband and wife on the auction-block, when you can see innocent children taken from their mothers and sold into eternal separation, I think it is not unnatural in me to fear that a woman with my convictions would not be happy mated with a Southerner.
10062-8{_}3973{_}All this is cruel, I fear you will think, but it would be crueller for me to encourage a love that, under present circumstances, would bring misery to both of us."
10062-8{_}3974{_}"You are an abolitionist?"
10062-8{_}3975{_}"Yes; every right-thinking person in the North is an abolitionist to this extent; we want the South to take the remedy into its own hands, to free its slaves voluntarily; the radical abolitionists prefer a violent means.
10062-8{_}3976{_}That I do not seek or did not; but now, Vincent, it is bound to come."
10062-8{_}3977{_}"And, if it should come, what would you answer to my question?"
10062-8{_}3978{_}"Here is a white rose: I picked it with my hand, and, you see, a drop of my blood is on it; when you can give me a rose with a drop of your blood on it as free from taint as the stain mine makes, I shall have an answer that will not be unworthy your waiting for!"
10062-8{_}3979{_}"Unworthy!
10062-8{_}3980{_}I don't understand you.
10062-8{_}3981{_}Surely, you don't think me a profligate?"
10062-8{_}3982{_}"When the time comes that no human being acknowledges your ownership, perhaps you may receive a voluntary bond-maid, bound to you by stronger ties than the chattel of the slave."
10062-8{_}3983{_}"But you love me, then, Olympia?"
10062-8{_}3984{_}"I can not love where I do not reverence."
10062-8{_}3985{_}"But it is not my fault that slaves are my inheritance!"
10062-8{_}3986{_}"It will be your fault if they are your support when you are your own master."
10062-8{_}3987{_}"You love an idea better than you love a man who would die for you!"
10062-8{_}3988{_}"I love manliness and the sense of right, which is called duty, better than I love a man who is blind to the first impulse of real manhood--"  "Would you ask a Jew to give up his synagogue to gain your hand?"
10062-8{_}3989{_}"The synagogue is the temple of a creed as divine as my own, and the faith of the man I loved would never swerve me in accepting or refusing him."
10062-8{_}3990{_}"We of the South believe slavery a divine institution--that is, first established by the fathers!"
10062-8{_}3991{_}"The tribes in the Fiji Islands believe man-eating an ordinance of the gods!"
10062-8{_}3992{_}"Well, this sort of discussion leads to nothing," Vincent said, ruefully.
10062-8{_}3993{_}"The world is well lost for the woman one loves, when I come to you shorn of my world!"
10062-8{_}3994{_}"Ah!
10062-8{_}3995{_}then, Vincent, you will find another!"
10062-8{_}3996{_}He drew her hand from the clinging vines and kissed it.
10062-8{_}3997{_}"I am very happy.
10062-8{_}3998{_}I shall lose my world with a very light heart."
10062-8{_}3999{_}"The world is a very tough brier; we sometimes bring it closer, when its thorns prick us more painfully in the struggles to cast it off."
10062-8{_}4000{_}"Then I'll cut the brambles, and not risk tearing my flesh!"
10062-8{_}4001{_}"That's the soldier's way--the heroic way; but wait for the future; I am young and you are not old."
10062-8{_}4002{_}Vincent's gayety when they returned to the drawing-room attracted the observant Dick, and he slyly whispered to the warrior, "Been practicing the Roman strategy with the Sabines?"
10062-8{_}4003{_}"No, I've been at the Temple of Minerva and taken a pledge to hold my tongue."
10062-8{_}4004{_}"Ah!
10062-8{_}4005{_}the goddess of the owls; but, as they see light only in darkness, I fear you groped in blackness."
10062-8{_}4006{_}The whole household were to meet President Davis and his party in Williamsburg, assist at the review, and get back with the distinguished guests in time for a state dinner.
10062-8{_}4007{_}Merry and Mrs. Sprague were reluctant to go, but they feared a refusal would be misunderstood.
10062-8{_}4008{_}Poor Merry was very tearful and disconsolate at the thought of leaving Dick, but she strove heroically to hide her grief when the cavalcade set out, the elder ladies driving, the young people mounted.
10062-8{_}4009{_}The ancient capital of Virginia was aflame with the new rebel bunting.
10062-8{_}4010{_}President Davis, with Generals Lee and Magruder, were in place on the pretty green before the old colonial college edifice when the Rosedale people came up.
10062-8{_}4011{_}Davis saluted Mrs. Atterbury with cordial urbanity; but, as the troops were already in column, there was only time for hasty presentation of the strangers.
10062-8{_}4012{_}Jack watched the rather piebald pageant with absorbed interest.
10062-8{_}4013{_}The infantry marched wretchedly.
10062-8{_}4014{_}The arms were as varied as the uniforms, and the artillery seemed a relic of Jackson's time.
10062-8{_}4015{_}But the cavalry was superb.
10062-8{_}4016{_}Never had he seen such splendid ranks, such noble horses.
10062-8{_}4017{_}At sight of the tall, elegant figure of the President, the troops broke into the peculiar shrill cheer that afterward became a sound of wonder, almost terror, to unaccustomed Northern ears.
10062-8{_}4018{_}It was a mingling of the boyish treble of college cries and the menacing shriek of the wild-cat.
10062-8{_}4019{_}Jack was secretly very much delighted with the review.
10062-8{_}4020{_}More than half the rank and file were mere boys; and he could see that they were unruly, almost to point-blank disregard of their officers commands, or the prescriptions of the manual.
10062-8{_}4021{_}It would take short work for the disciplined hosts the new Northern general was training, to sweep such chaff from the field of war.
10062-8{_}4022{_}Vincent saw something of this in his comrade's eye, and a good deal nettled himself by the slovenly march and humorous abandon of the men, he said:  "You must remember, Jack, our army is made up of gentlemen's sons; the gentry of the South are all in arms, and we can't at once reduce them to the mere machines a more heterogeneous soldiery can be made.
10062-8{_}4023{_}The men who won Manassas passed in review a day or two before the battle, and they made the same impression upon me--upon Beauregard himself--that I see these men have made on you.
10062-8{_}4024{_}Depend upon it, in a fight they will be good soldiers."
10062-8{_}4025{_}"Let me have the poor comfort of underrating my enemy, the thing above all others that a wise man shuns and a fool indulges."
10062-8{_}4026{_}"Oh, on that theory revile them if you like."
10062-8{_}4027{_}"No, indeed; I'm far from reviling them.
10062-8{_}4028{_}The cavalry is magnificent.
10062-8{_}4029{_}I don't think we have a regiment in our army that can compare with that brigade.
10062-8{_}4030{_}Who commands it?"
10062-8{_}4031{_}"Jeb Stuart--the Murat of the South," Vincent said, proudly.
10062-8{_}4032{_}"I'm going to tell the President what you said of the brigade; you know he is passionately fond of the army, and really wanted to be the commander-in-chief, when they made him President at Montgomery."
10062-8{_}4033{_}At sunset the President and General Lee entered the carriage with Mrs. Atterbury and Mrs. Sprague, Merry driving in a phaeton with Kate, who didn't enjoy so long a ride on the horse.
10062-8{_}4034{_}"I'm glad we've got such important hostages as yourself and son," Davis said gallantly to Mrs. Sprague, as the carriage passed out of the clamor of acclamation the crowd set up.
10062-8{_}4035{_}"I knew the Senator, your husband, intimately.
10062-8{_}4036{_}If he had lived, I doubt whether we should have been driven out of the Union.
10062-8{_}4037{_}He was, in my mind, one of the most prudent statesmen that came from the North to Congress."
10062-8{_}4038{_}"He certainly never would have consented to break up the Union," Mrs. Sprague said, in embarrassment.
10062-8{_}4039{_}"Nor should I, madam, if there had been any further security in it.
10062-8{_}4040{_}The truth is, there was nothing left for us but to go out or be kicked out.
10062-8{_}4041{_}The leaders of the Abolition party long ago proclaimed that.
10062-8{_}4042{_}However, war settles all such problems.
10062-8{_}4043{_}When it is settled by the sword we shall be satisfied."
10062-8{_}4044{_}Mrs. Atterbury changed the conversation by asking how Mrs. Davis liked Richmond.
10062-8{_}4045{_}"Oh, she has been treated royally by the people there.
10062-8{_}4046{_}I declare Richmond is as Southern a city as Charleston.
10062-8{_}4047{_}I have been agreeably surprised by the absolute unanimity of gentle and simple in the cause.
10062-8{_}4048{_}My wife receives a clothes-basketful of letters every morning from the mothers of the Confederacy proffering time, money, and service wherever she can suggest anything for them to do.
10062-8{_}4049{_}I propose later on establishing an order something like the Golden Fleece, which shall confer a certain social precedence upon the wearers.
10062-8{_}4050{_}I have thousands of letters on the subject, and as the society of the South is, as a matter of fact, a society of gentle-folk--for the most part lineally descended from the nobility of older countries--I think it proper and right that lineage should have certain acknowledged advantages in the new commonwealth.
10062-8{_}4051{_}But I propose to go further, and institute an order of something like nobility for women--who have thus far given us great help and encouragement.
10062-8{_}4052{_}Indeed, there are many in the Congress--a dozen Senators I could name--who think that we ought to make our regime entirely different from the North, and that we should adopt a monarchical form--"  "I'm sure, I think we should," Mrs. Atterbury exclaimed, delightedly.
10062-8{_}4053{_}"We are really as unlike the Northern people as the French or the Germans."
10062-8{_}4054{_}"The strongest argument for declaring the Confederacy an empire is the one that weighed with Napoleon I.
10062-8{_}4055{_}We should at one stroke secure the alliance of all the monarchies.
10062-8{_}4056{_}They have never looked with favor on the experiment of a powerful republic over here, and it is almost certain they would befriend us for transforming this mighty infant state into an empire.
10062-8{_}4057{_}However, that is for future action.
10062-8{_}4058{_}Our agents abroad have sent us full reports on the matter."
10062-8{_}4059{_}"I doubt the wisdom of ever hinting such a thing," General Lee said, gravely.
10062-8{_}4060{_}"We must show that we are able to act independently in selecting our form of government.
10062-8{_}4061{_}I doubt very much whether the masses would listen favorably to an empire established by foreign aid."
10062-8{_}4062{_}"Possibly, general, possibly.
10062-8{_}4063{_}As I said before, there will be time enough for that when, like Napoleon, we have made our armies the masters of this continent.
10062-8{_}4064{_}Then, with boundaries embracing Mexico, Canada, and the Western States--for they can never exist independent of us--we can choose empire, republic, or a Venetian oligarchy."
10062-8{_}4065{_}As they came in sight of Rosedale, Davis stood up in the carriage to get a better view of the landscape, which showed swift alternations of dense thickets and wood and rolling acres of rich crops.
10062-8{_}4066{_}"What a State Virginia is!"
10062-8{_}4067{_}he exclaimed with enthusiasm.
10062-8{_}4068{_}"It has the climate and soil to support half of Europe.
10062-8{_}4069{_}Mother of Presidents in the past, it will be the granary and magazine of the Confederacy in ten years.
10062-8{_}4070{_}My own State, Mississippi, is rich in land, but the climate is hard for the stranger.
10062-8{_}4071{_}It enervates the European at first.
10062-8{_}4072{_}But we are an agricultural people, or rather we give our energies to our staple, cotton; that is to be the chief treasure of the Confederacy."
10062-8{_}4073{_}Dinner was ready for the table when the guests came from their rooms.
10062-8{_}4074{_}Davis excused his lack of ceremonial dress, saying pleasantly:  "I am something of a soldier, you know, and travel with a light train.
10062-8{_}4075{_}Lee, there, has the advantage of me.
10062-8{_}4076{_}A soldier's uniform is court costume the world over."
10062-8{_}4077{_}"But you are the commander-in-chief, Mr. President.
10062-8{_}4078{_}Don't you have a uniform?"
10062-8{_}4079{_}"No.
10062-8{_}4080{_}I am commander-in-chief only in law.
10062-8{_}4081{_}Congress is really the commander-in-chief.
10062-8{_}4082{_}The man that assumes those duties can attend to them alone.
10062-8{_}4083{_}He is, of course, subject to the executive; but only in general plans, rarely in details."
10062-8{_}4084{_}Davis was placed at Mrs. Atterbury's right, Mrs. Sprague at her left, General Lee sat at Vincent's right, _vis-à-vis_ to Jack, who was lost in prodigious admiration of the Socratic-like chieftain--Lee was as yet unknown to all but a discriminating few in the Confederacy.
10062-8{_}4085{_}He was as tall as Davis fully six feet--but more rounded and symmetrical.
10062-8{_}4086{_}He spoke with great gravity, but seemed to enjoy the jests that the young people found opportunities to indulge in, when it was seen that the President devoted his talk exclusively to the hostess or Mrs. Sprague.
10062-8{_}4087{_}Davis was a good talker, and charmed the company with reminiscences of old times in Congress.
10062-8{_}4088{_}"I don't remember Lincoln distinctly," he said, concluding a reminiscence, "but I think he's the man that used to be so popular in the House cloak-room, telling stories which were said to be extremely droll."
10062-8{_}4089{_}"Mrs. Lincoln is in some sort kin to Mrs. Davis, isn't she?"
10062-8{_}4090{_}Mrs. Atterbury asked.
10062-8{_}4091{_}"I have read it somewhere."
10062-8{_}4092{_}"Very distant.
10062-8{_}4093{_}Mrs. Lincoln is of the Kentucky Tods, and they were in some way kin of my wife's family, the Howells.
10062-8{_}4094{_}Not enough to put on mourning, if Mrs. Lincoln should become a widow."
10062-8{_}4095{_}"Is it true, Mr. President, that a society in the North has offered a million dollars for your capture--abduction?
10062-8{_}4096{_}I heard it in Williamsburg, and saw an allusion to it in _The Examiner_ the other day."
10062-8{_}4097{_}"Oh, I'm sure I can't say.
10062-8{_}4098{_}If the offer were authenticated, I should be tempted to go and get the reward myself.
10062-8{_}4099{_}With a million dollars I could do a good deal more for the cause in the North than I can here, making brigadiers and settling questions of precedence between Cabinet ministers, judges, and Senators."
10062-8{_}4100{_}"Mr. President, give me an exchange North, and I will ascertain the facts in the million-dollar offer and write you faithfully how to set about getting the money," Jack said, very soberly, from his end of the table.
10062-8{_}4101{_}"Ah!
10062-8{_}4102{_}the Yankee spoke there--nothing if not a bargain.
10062-8{_}4103{_}Sir, you deserve your clearance papers, but I'm too good a friend of Mrs. Atterbury and her daughter to bring about the loss of company that I am sure must be agreeable.
10062-8{_}4104{_}Then, too, there's no telling the miracles of conversion that may be brought about by such ministers as Miss Rosa there."
10062-8{_}4105{_}Rosa blushed, Jack felt foolish, and everybody laughed except Dick, who looked unutterable things at his adored, and boldly entered the lists against the great personage by asking, in a quivering treble:  "Doesn't the Bible say that the wife shall cleave to the husband; that his people shall be her people, his God her God, where he goes she goes?"
10062-8{_}4106{_}"It is so said in the Bible, sir; but it was a woman that uttered it, and she was in love.
10062-8{_}4107{_}When you know more of the sex, you will understand that women in love are like poets; they say much that they don't mean, and more that they don't understand."
10062-8{_}4108{_}"But, Mr. President, what the one woman said in the Bible all women practice.
10062-8{_}4109{_}You never knew a woman that didn't believe her husband's beliefs, hate his hates, love his loves."
10062-8{_}4110{_}Davis smiled, and his eyes twinkled kindly on his boyish inquisitor.
10062-8{_}4111{_}"I know only one woman.
10062-8{_}4112{_}That is as much as a man can speak for.
10062-8{_}4113{_}She doesn't hate my hates, love my loves, or enter unprotestingly into all my ways.
10062-8{_}4114{_}Indeed, I may say that, being a peaceful man, I wanted to remain in Washington, for I believed that Seward was sincere in pleading for a compromise; but the woman I speak of had her own opinion convinced me that she was right, and I came to my own people."
10062-8{_}4115{_}At this moment there was a diversion.
10062-8{_}4116{_}A soldier, booted and spurred, entered the room, walked to the head of the table, and bending deferentially to the President, said;  "I am ordered to deliver this message wherever you may be found."
10062-8{_}4117{_}He handed Davis a large envelope and retreated respectfully two or three paces backward.
10062-8{_}4118{_}Everybody affected to resume conversation as the President, breaking the seal, said;  "Pardon me a moment, madam."
10062-8{_}4119{_}But he had no sooner ran over the lines than he turned to the courier, crying, in visible discomfiture:  "When did you leave the war office?"
10062-8{_}4120{_}"At five o'clock, sir."
10062-8{_}4121{_}"General, we must return instantly to Richmond; a hundred or more of the prisoners have broken out of Libby!
10062-8{_}4122{_}It is reported that a column of the enemy with gunboats have passed up the James.--Madam, this is one of the exigencies of a time of war.
10062-8{_}4123{_}I needn't say to an Atterbury that everything must give way to public business!"
10062-8{_}4124{_}He called Lee aside, spoke rapidly to him, and the latter, beckoning Vincent, left the room.
10062-8{_}4125{_}He returned in ten minutes, announcing that everything was in readiness to set out.
10062-8{_}4126{_}The carriage with Mrs. Sprague's and Merry's small luggage was ready when the cavalcade set out, Davis riding with them and the cavalry company from below, divided into squadrons before and behind the carriage.
10062-8{_}4127{_}It was eleven o'clock as the last dark line of the troop disappeared.
10062-8{_}4128{_}Olympia and Jack stood at the great gate in mournful silence.
10062-8{_}4129{_}The swiftness of the parting had lessened the pain, but their minds were full of the sorrow that follows the inevitable.
10062-8{_}4130{_}Mrs. Sprague had herself declined to postpone the ordeal when Mrs. Atterbury pointed out the untimely hour.
10062-8{_}4131{_}No, it was better to suffer this slight inconvenience to have Vincent's protecting presence all the way to the Union lines; and Jack, acknowledging this, didn't say a word to dissuade her.
10062-8{_}4132{_}Vincent's last act was to call Jack to his room.
10062-8{_}4133{_}"I wanted to tell you, Jack, what a great joy it has been to me--it has been to all of us--to have you in our home at this trying time.
10062-8{_}4134{_}I can not tell you how much comfort it has been to me now, but some time you shall know," Vincent stammered, and began to open a drawer in the bureau.
10062-8{_}4135{_}"Here is something I want you to accept as a keepsake from me."
10062-8{_}4136{_}He drew forth a pistol-case and opened it.
10062-8{_}4137{_}"It will be a melancholy pleasure for me to feel, in the dark days to come, that these weapons may prove your friend in battle, where I must be your enemy."
10062-8{_}4138{_}"By George, they're beauties!"
10062-8{_}4139{_}Jack cried, taking the weapons out.
10062-8{_}4140{_}"Yes; they were bought last year, and I have had J.S.
10062-8{_}4141{_}cut on one, and V.A.
10062-8{_}4142{_}on the other.
10062-8{_}4143{_}I meant them for your Christmas last year, but they were mislaid."
10062-8{_}4144{_}"What a kind fellow you are, Vint!
10062-8{_}4145{_}I don't think I ought to take these."
10062-8{_}4146{_}"Why not?
10062-8{_}4147{_}I have others!
10062-8{_}4148{_}I shall feel easier, knowing that you have them.
10062-8{_}4149{_}You can stow them about you easily, they are so small."
10062-8{_}4150{_}"But it's against the laws of war for a prisoner to be armed."
10062-8{_}4151{_}"That's just the reason I haven't asked you to take them before.
10062-8{_}4152{_}You can leave them here in my room until you are exchanged, and then you can carry them with impunity."
10062-8{_}4153{_}The household assembled at the gate leading into the roadway as the cavalcade took up the march.
10062-8{_}4154{_}There were sad, sobbing farewells spoken--the kindly night covering the tears, and the loud neighing of the horses drowning the sobs.
10062-8{_}4155{_}The Northern group remained in the roadway, straining their eyes to catch the last glimpse of the wanderers as they disappeared in the misty foliage, far up the roadway.
10062-8{_}4156{_}The horizon to the zenith was full of shimmering star-points, Olympia, with Jack, turned slowly toward the house, silent and not wholly sad.
10062-8{_}4157{_}Dick, in a low treble, could be heard just behind them, quoting melancholy verses to Rosa; and the brother and sister returned slowly up the dewy, odorous path.
10062-8{_}4158{_}At the porch Rosa exclaimed, in surprise:  "I wonder where Pizarro is?
10062-8{_}4159{_}I haven't seen him while we have been out.
10062-8{_}4160{_}It can't be possible he has followed Vincent!
10062-8{_}4161{_}What shall we do if he has?"
10062-8{_}4162{_}"Make Dick take his place.
10062-8{_}4163{_}A terrier is sometimes as faithful as a mastiff," Jack said, quickly.
10062-8{_}4164{_}"Oh!
10062-8{_}4165{_}Miss Atterbury wants something with a bite, rather than a bark, and a terrier wouldn't do," the boy answered.
10062-8{_}4166{_}"I want Pizarro.
10062-8{_}4167{_}I shall never sleep a wink all night if he isn't here," Rosa said, in consternation; "he is better than a regiment of soldiers, for he won't let a human being come near the house after the doors are closed, not even the servants."
10062-8{_}4168{_}An expedition, calling upon Pizarro in many keys, set out and wandered through the grounds, back to the quarters, to the gates leading to the rose-fields, to the stable, but Pizarro was not to be found.
10062-8{_}4169{_}Lights were burning in the hall only when the four re-entered, and with a very grave face Rosa bade the rest good-night.
10062-8{_}4170{_}CHAPTER XX.
10062-8{_}4171{_}A CATASTROPHE.
10062-8{_}4172{_}Rosedale had been a bed of thorns to Wesley Boone since his recovery.
10062-8{_}4173{_}He felt that he was an incongruous visitor among the rest, as a hawk might feel in a dove-cote.
10062-8{_}4174{_}He would have willingly returned to Richmond--even at the risk of re-entering the prison--if Kate had not been on his hands.
10062-8{_}4175{_}The life of the place, the constant necessity of masking his aversion to the Spragues, his detestation of Dick, the simple merry-making and intimate amenities of such close quarters, tasked his small art of dissimulation beyond even the most practiced powers.
10062-8{_}4176{_}The garment of duplicity was gossamer, he felt, after all, in such atmosphere of loyalty and trust as surrounded him at Rosedale.
10062-8{_}4177{_}He knew that in the daily attrition and conventional intimacies of the table, the drawing-room, or the promenade, the cloak covering his resentful antipathy, his moral perversities, his thinly veiled impatience, was worn to such thin shreds that eyes keen as Jack's must see and know him as he was.
10062-8{_}4178{_}What was hatefulest and most unendurable of all was the bondage of truce in which the Atterburys held him.
10062-8{_}4179{_}Wesley was no coward, and he ached to meet Jack face to face, arm to arm, and settle with that thoughtless insubordinate a rankling list of griefs heaped up in moments of over-vivacious frankness.
10062-8{_}4180{_}He would make Jack smart for his arrogance, his insolence, his cursed condescension so soon as they were back among the Caribees.
10062-8{_}4181{_}But meanwhile, here, daily tortured by harmless things--tortured by his soul's imaginings--Wesley was becoming a burden to Kate, who saw too plainly that he was in misery, and realized that it was largely through his own inherent weakness and insincerity.
10062-8{_}4182{_}He had all the coarse fiber of his father without the same force in its texture.
10062-8{_}4183{_}With merely superficial good manners, he was never certain whether the punctilious niceties observed toward him by the Spragues and Atterburys were not a species of studied satire.
10062-8{_}4184{_}Vincent, who had never shown him the slightest consideration in Acredale, treated him here with the chivalrous decorum that the code of the South demanded in those days to a guest.
10062-8{_}4185{_}Wesley ground his teeth under the burden, not quite sure whether it was mockery or malevolence.
10062-8{_}4186{_}He watched with malignant attentiveness the imperceptible change of tone and manner that marked the family's treatment of the Spragues.
10062-8{_}4187{_}There was none of the grave ceremoniousness he resented in the Atterburys' behavior with them.
10062-8{_}4188{_}Jack was a hobbledehoy son of the house, almost as much as Vincent.
10062-8{_}4189{_}Kate, too, was, he felt certain, treated with a reserve not shown to Mrs. Sprague or Merry.
10062-8{_}4190{_}Brooding on this, brooding on the unhappiness of his own disposition, which denied him the privilege of enjoying the best at the moment, indifferent to what might be behind, Wesley had come to hate the Atterburys for the burden of an obligation that he could never lift.
10062-8{_}4191{_}He hated Mrs. Atterbury for her high-bred, easy ignoring of all conditions save those that she exacted.
10062-8{_}4192{_}He hated Rosa for her gayety, her absorption in the young scamp Dick.
10062-8{_}4193{_}He hated Vincent because he seemed to think there was no one in the North but the Spragues worthy of a moment's consideration.
10062-8{_}4194{_}It is in hate as in love--what we seek we find.
10062-8{_}4195{_}Every innocent word and sign that passed in the group, in which he did not seek to make himself one, Wesley construed as a gird at him or his family.
10062-8{_}4196{_}Constantly on the watch for slights or disparagements, the most thoughtless acts of the two groups were taken by the tormented egotist as in some sense a disparagement to his own good repute or his family standing.
10062-8{_}4197{_}Nor were the marked affection and confidence shown Kate by everybody in the house a mitigation of this malign fabric of humiliation.
10062-8{_}4198{_}Jack's fondness for Kate had not escaped the observant eyes of Dick, who had confided the secret to Rosa, who had likewise unraveled it to mamma, and, as she kept nothing from Vincent, the Atterburys had that sort of interest in Kate that intimate spectators always show in love affairs, where there are no clashing interests involved.
10062-8{_}4199{_}It was a moot question, however, between the three, when, after weeks of observation, Mrs. Atterbury declared that Jack was not in love with Miss Boone.
10062-8{_}4200{_}"He can't be," she declared.
10062-8{_}4201{_}"He doesn't seek her alone; he doesn't make up to her in the evening.
10062-8{_}4202{_}Half the time when they come together it is by Dick's arrangement.
10062-8{_}4203{_}_He_ seems to be in love with Kate."
10062-8{_}4204{_}"How absurd!"
10062-8{_}4205{_}Rosa cried, with a laugh; "a boy like him!
10062-8{_}4206{_}Why, he would be in school, if there were no war."
10062-8{_}4207{_}"Well, Rosa, I fancy that Dick hasn't found war very much different from school, so far.
10062-8{_}4208{_}He seems to recite a good deal to the mistress, and occupies the dunce's block quite regularly," Vincent retorted, with a provoking significance that set mamma in a brown study and suspended the comments on Kate's and Jack's probable sentiments.
10062-8{_}4209{_}Mrs. Sprague and Wesley were the only people in the house who had no suspicion of a deeper feeling than mere passing goodfellowship between Jack and Kate.
10062-8{_}4210{_}Both were blinded by the same confidence.
10062-8{_}4211{_}The mother could never conceive a son of the house of Sprague making such a breach on the family traditions as a union with a Boone.
10062-8{_}4212{_}Wesley could not conceive a sister of his giving her heart to the son of a family that had insolently refused to concede social equality to her father.
10062-8{_}4213{_}Something of Wesley's miserable inner unrest could not fail to be visible to the Atterburys, but the less congenial he became the more watchfully considerate they made their treatment of him.
10062-8{_}4214{_}He was their guest, with all the sacred rights and immunities that quality implies, in the exaggerated code of the Southern host.
10062-8{_}4215{_}Kate was the single power that Wesley had bent his headstrong will before, ever since he was a boy.
10062-8{_}4216{_}His father he obeyed, while in his presence, trusting to wheedling to make his peace in the event of disobedience.
10062-8{_}4217{_}But Kate he couldn't wheedle.
10062-8{_}4218{_}She was relentless in her scorn for his meannesses and follies, and, though he did not always heed her counsels, he proved their justness by finding his own course wrong.
10062-8{_}4219{_}Kate, however, hesitated about remonstrating with him on his deepening moodiness, for she was not quite sure whether it was mad jealousy of Dick's favor in Rosa's eyes, or a secret purpose to attempt to fly from the gentle bondage of Rosedale.
10062-8{_}4220{_}Wesley with Rosa it was remarked by Kate, was, or seemed to be, his better self, or rather better than the self with which others identified him.
10062-8{_}4221{_}It was, however, she feared, more to torment Dick, than because she found Wesley to her liking, that the little maid often carried the moody captain off into the garden, pretending to teach him the varied flora of that blooming domain.
10062-8{_}4222{_}Dick remarked these excursions with growing impatience, and visited his anger upon Rosa in protests so pungent and woe-begone that she was forced to own to him that she only pretended an interest in the captain, so that he might not think he was shut out of the confidence of the circle.
10062-8{_}4223{_}"And who cares if he does think he is shut out, I should like to know?
10062-8{_}4224{_}He is a sneak, and I don't like to have you talking with him alone," Dick cries, quite in the tone of the Benedict who has passed the marriage-portal and feels safe to make his will known.
10062-8{_}4225{_}"I should like to know what right you have to order what I shall or shall not do?"
10062-8{_}4226{_}Rosa protests, half angry, half laughing.
10062-8{_}4227{_}"Why, you talk like a grown man--like a husband.
10062-8{_}4228{_}How dare you?"
10062-8{_}4229{_}Dick pauses confused, and looks guiltily about at this.
10062-8{_}4230{_}"Ah, if you put it that way I have no right except this: My whole heart is yours.
10062-8{_}4231{_}You know that.
10062-8{_}4232{_}You may not have given me all yours."
10062-8{_}4233{_}(Protesting shrug from Rosa's shoulders.)
10062-8{_}4234{_}"Well, all the same; if my heart is all your own you have a duty in the case.
10062-8{_}4235{_}You ought to spare your own property from pain."
10062-8{_}4236{_}(Rosa laughs softly.)
10062-8{_}4237{_}"Of course you are right.
10062-8{_}4238{_}You are always right.
