10062-8{_}6750{_}Jack Sprague has gone over to the rebels, just as Anderson and his men went over at Sumter; just as fifteen hundred of his comrades went over at Bull Run; just as some of our sons and brothers here in Acredale went over; just as my friend, Boone's son, went over--because he was surrounded and wounded."
10062-8{_}6751{_}"Stop a moment, if you please, friend Brodie; I protest against your making anything in common between my son and this young man.
10062-8{_}6752{_}The matter is to be investigated, and then we can tell better."
10062-8{_}6753{_}Boone spoke in great excitement, and the audience, now feverishly wrought up, urged the lawyer to say his say out.
10062-8{_}6754{_}He continued in the trained, impassive tones of the advocate:  "Every one in this room knows the two young men.
10062-8{_}6755{_}It would be waste of time for me to strive to make anything in common between John Sprague and Wesley Boone.
10062-8{_}6756{_}Here, where they both grew up, that is quite unnecessary."
10062-8{_}6757{_}"I--I--referred to their conduct as soldiers," Boone cried, hoarsely.
10062-8{_}6758{_}"My son lost his life in the service of his country.
10062-8{_}6759{_}I can't have his name coupled with a--murderer's--with a traitor's."
10062-8{_}6760{_}"Ah, my friend, when hate draws your portrait it is bound to be black.
10062-8{_}6761{_}When prejudice holds the pen, your virtues stand in the shade of vice.
10062-8{_}6762{_}I will tell John Sprague's story from the day he quit Acredale to the unhappy hour his comrade was killed in the dark, in the sleeping-room of the mother and daughter who had nursed him from the very jaws of death.
10062-8{_}6763{_}He was in that house by his father's urgent request, though it would have needed none to open its doors to any one in want of succor.
10062-8{_}6764{_}Nor," he added, significantly, "can it be told who killed Wesley Boone until all the shots fired in Mrs. Atterbury's chamber are accounted for."
10062-8{_}6765{_}Then he narrated rapidly, but tellingly, the substance of what has been already set down in this history--the facts taken from Jack's letters and attested by the corroboration of Barney, Dick, and the company's officers.
10062-8{_}6766{_}There was a visible revulsion in the larger part of the audience as the tale went on; and when the lawyer wound up with the story of Mrs. Sprague's baffled efforts in Washington to have her boy brought North, there was an outburst of applause and a faint cheer from the younger men for "glorious old Jack."
10062-8{_}6767{_}The factions shifted a good deal after this official rendering of the affair.
10062-8{_}6768{_}There was no longer any talk of burning the Sprague property, and opinion was about evenly divided as to Jack's conduct.
10062-8{_}6769{_}December had come, and the township was busy packing boxes to send to the army.
10062-8{_}6770{_}No news had come North from Richmond.
10062-8{_}6771{_}Active movements were looked for every day, and in the momentous expectation such lesser incidents as exchange were forgotten or ignored.
10062-8{_}6772{_}The daily journals were filled with details of contemplated expeditions, and one morning Mrs. Sprague read with beating heart this paragraph in the _Herald_:  "A score or more of the men who escaped from the Richmond prison a few weeks ago, arrived at Washington to-day from Fort Monroe.
10062-8{_}6773{_}The party endured untold privations in the swamps between Williamsburg and our line on the Warwick, but all came in safely, except two men who died from the results of their wounds.
10062-8{_}6774{_}The expedition was planned and carried out by an agent of General Butler, who has been in Virginia since the unfortunate attempt to rescue Captain Boone of the 'Caribee' regiment.
10062-8{_}6775{_}At the moment the party reached the Union outpost, one of the most daring of the Union men, Sergeant Jacques of the Caribees, was, it is thought, mortally wounded."
10062-8{_}6776{_}Merry, too, had seen the story, and came over to show it to Mrs. Sprague.
10062-8{_}6777{_}"I have seen it, I have seen it.
10062-8{_}6778{_}Who of the Caribees can these be?
10062-8{_}6779{_}Who is Jacques?
10062-8{_}6780{_}I never heard that name here."
10062-8{_}6781{_}"Ah!
10062-8{_}6782{_}he must be one of the town recruits.
10062-8{_}6783{_}It's a French name."
10062-8{_}6784{_}"Yes, it is part of a rather famous French name," Mrs. Sprague replied, half smiling at Merry's innocence.
10062-8{_}6785{_}"Something must be done to get into communication with these escaped men.
10062-8{_}6786{_}Some of them must have seen Jack.
10062-8{_}6787{_}If there are Caribees among them, you may be sure they have messages from our boys.
10062-8{_}6788{_}I think I shall set out for Washington, or ask Mr. Brodie to go."
10062-8{_}6789{_}"That's better.
10062-8{_}6790{_}Mr. Brodie can get at the men and you couldn't.
10062-8{_}6791{_}I shall be in a fever until we have heard from them."
10062-8{_}6792{_}Brodie agreed with the ladies when, later, they discussed the matter with him, and that evening he set out for Washington.
10062-8{_}6793{_}Mrs. Sprague at the tea-table with Merry, who made it a point to give the lonely mother as much of her time as she could spare, was still pondering the paragraph when the sound of carriage-wheels came in through the closed curtains.
10062-8{_}6794{_}Then the front door opened without knocking, and there was a rustle in the hallway, and then, with a simultaneous scream, three agitated females, to wit, Mrs. Sprague, Merry, and Olympia, in a confused mass.
10062-8{_}6795{_}"O my child!
10062-8{_}6796{_}my child!"
10062-8{_}6797{_}"Mamma!"
10062-8{_}6798{_}"Dearest, dearest Olympia," Merry splutters, wildly embracing both.
10062-8{_}6799{_}"Oh, how delightful to be here, to see you, mamma as peaceful and serene as in the old days!
10062-8{_}6800{_}I thought I should never get home.
10062-8{_}6801{_}I left Richmond three weeks ago.
10062-8{_}6802{_}I was held at Fredericksburg for ten days.
10062-8{_}6803{_}Then I had to turn back when we got to Manassas, through some red tape lacking there.
10062-8{_}6804{_}But here I am.
10062-8{_}6805{_}Here I am at home--ugh!--I shall never quit it again--never."
10062-8{_}6806{_}"But, my child.
10062-8{_}6807{_}Tell us--Jack!"
10062-8{_}6808{_}"Jack?
10062-8{_}6809{_}Haven't you heard from him?
10062-8{_}6810{_}He escaped three weeks ago.
10062-8{_}6811{_}It was he who got the men out of the prison.
10062-8{_}6812{_}Dick was with him.
10062-8{_}6813{_}Surely you have heard of that?"
10062-8{_}6814{_}and Olympia sank into the nearest chair, all the gayety gone from her face, her eyes questioning the two wretched women.
10062-8{_}6815{_}Neither could for the moment control her agitation; neither was capable of thinking.
10062-8{_}6816{_}All that was in their minds was this dire specter of a month's silence.
10062-8{_}6817{_}Alive, Jack or Dick would have found means to relieve their anxiety.
10062-8{_}6818{_}"Surely you heard that a party had escaped from Libby and made their way to Fort Monroe?"
10062-8{_}6819{_}Olympia cried, desperately.
10062-8{_}6820{_}"Fort Monroe?"
10062-8{_}6821{_}Mrs. Sprague echoed mechanically.
10062-8{_}6822{_}"Yes, ah, yes.
10062-8{_}6823{_}Merry, where's the paper?"
10062-8{_}6824{_}Olympia devoured the meager scrap and then dropped the journal on her knees.
10062-8{_}6825{_}Her mind was in a whirl.
10062-8{_}6826{_}In Richmond the escape had been announced, then the news that the party had been surrounded in the swamp, then day by day details of the taking of straggling negroes and one or two soldiers, but no name that even resembled Jack's.
10062-8{_}6827{_}The Atterburys, after the first painful sensation, had given their approval of Jack's going, and used all means in their power to get such facts as would comfort Olympia.
10062-8{_}6828{_}They assured her that Jack had reached the Union lines, and then she had set out northward, expecting to find him at home or in communication with his family.
10062-8{_}6829{_}No word from Dick?
10062-8{_}6830{_}No word from Jack?
10062-8{_}6831{_}They were dead, and she--she had urged them to the mad adventure!
10062-8{_}6832{_}She had given Jack no peace, had fired Dick to the fatal enterprise.
10062-8{_}6833{_}She dared not look in the tearless eyes of her mother.
10062-8{_}6834{_}She dared not face the ghastly questioning in Merry's meek eye.
10062-8{_}6835{_}Brodie had gone down to see the escaped men.
10062-8{_}6836{_}Perhaps he would discover something.
10062-8{_}6837{_}This was the small comfort left the three when, near midnight, they ended the woful conference.
10062-8{_}6838{_}The next day Olympia was visited by a representative of the _Crossbow_, the chief journal of Warchester, and urged to write a narrative of her adventures in the rebel capital.
10062-8{_}6839{_}Until her friends made her see how much effect it would have in clearing Jack's reputation she shrank from the publicity, but with that end in view--Jack's honor--she wrote, and wrote with strength and clearness, the moving incidents of her brother's capture, captivity, and escape--or his bold effort to escape.
10062-8{_}6840{_}This she told so simply, so directly, so vividly, that the truth of it at once, struck the most prejudiced reader, who had no cause to continue in his prepossession.
10062-8{_}6841{_}After the publication in the Warchester paper scores who had sided with the Boone faction either called or wrote to confess their error.
10062-8{_}6842{_}Even the Acredale _Monitor_, a weekly sheet notoriously in the interest of Boone, felt constrained to copy parts of the account and publish with it a shambling retraction of previous criticism, based on imperfect knowledge, that it had printed concerning Sergeant Sprague.
10062-8{_}6843{_}"Death," it declared, "has obliterated all feeling that existed against our young townsman, whose conduct, though open to grievous doubt in the early part of his military career has been amply atoned for in the intrepid enterprise in which he seems to have lost his life."
10062-8{_}6844{_}CHAPTER XXIX.
10062-8{_}6845{_}A WOMAN'S REASON.
10062-8{_}6846{_}The still, small voice that makes itself a force in the heart, which the poets call our mentor and the moralists conscience, had been painfully garrulous in Kate Boone's breast since the angry parting with Jack at Rosedale.
10062-8{_}6847{_}At first, in the wild grief of Wesley's death, she had hugged hatred of Jack to her heart as a sublime revenge for the murder.
10062-8{_}6848{_}But with the hot partisanship allayed in the long weeks of reflection preceding the rumor of Jack's own death, she began dimly to admit of palliation in her lover's fatal act.
10062-8{_}6849{_}Her father, the Boone faction, all who had access to her, held the shooting to be a craftily planned murder, calculated to bring advantage to the assassin.
10062-8{_}6850{_}To check the sacrilegious love she felt in her heart, she too had been forced to believe, to admit the worst.
10062-8{_}6851{_}But when the image of Jack came to her mind, as it did day and night, it was as the gay, frank, chivalrous Hotspur, as unlike a murderer as Golgotha to Hesperides.
10062-8{_}6852{_}She had never dared to confide to her father that vows had been exchanged between, them--that they were, in fact, affianced lovers.
10062-8{_}6853{_}He, never suspecting, talked with her day after day of the signal vengeance in store for the miscreant; how he had enlisted the aid of the most powerful in Washington; how he had instructed the emissaries sent to Richmond to effect Wesley's release, to direct all their energies to entrapping the murderer into the ranks of the escaping prisoners.
10062-8{_}6854{_}She had often been startled by her father's far-seeing, malignantly planned vengeances, and, now that the rumor of Jack's death began to settle into belief, she was appalled by a sudden sense of complicity in a murderous plot.
10062-8{_}6855{_}Not that she believed her father capable of murder or its procuration, but, knowing his potency with the authorities, she saw that there were many ways in which Jack might be sacrificed in the natural course of military duties.
10062-8{_}6856{_}She had heard things of the sort discussed--how inconvenient men had been sent into pitfalls and never heard of again.
10062-8{_}6857{_}She began dimly to see that, at worst, Jack's act was not the calculated murder her father held it to be.
10062-8{_}6858{_}In her own tortured mind there had been at first but one clear process of reasoning.
10062-8{_}6859{_}That process, whenever she began to gather the shreds, had led her mind straight to the conviction that Jack's shot had been premeditated, that the chance had been prearranged with the enemies of her brother.
10062-8{_}6860{_}At first her only distinct thought was that the hapless Wesley had been lured to his death.
10062-8{_}6861{_}The hand of the man she loved had sent the fatal shot into the poor boy's body.
10062-8{_}6862{_}Had it been in self-defense--even in the heat of uncontrollable anger--she could have found mitigation for Jack; but there was neither the justification of self-defense nor the plausible pretext of anger.
10062-8{_}6863{_}One word of warning, which Jack could have spoken, would have saved Wesley from the rash, the dastardly attempt upon the Rosedale household.
10062-8{_}6864{_}The plot, in all its details, must have been known to Jack or Dick, else how explain their presence in the chamber, armed and ready for the murder?
10062-8{_}6865{_}It had been a conspiracy of delusive kindness from the day Wesley entered Rosedale.
10062-8{_}6866{_}The frankness and kindliness of the Atterburys had been assumed to lure him to his fatal adventure.
10062-8{_}6867{_}Boone himself believed that Jack's ignoble ambition and envy had been the main motives in the murder.
10062-8{_}6868{_}To this Kate, from the first, opposed a resolute incredulity.
10062-8{_}6869{_}"You don't know the fellow, I tell you," Boone doggedly argued.
10062-8{_}6870{_}"He's as like his father as two snakes in a hole.
10062-8{_}6871{_}Old man Sprague never let a man stand in his way.
10062-8{_}6872{_}Jack's the same.
10062-8{_}6873{_}He thought Wes' kept him from the shoulder-straps, and he got him out of the way.
10062-8{_}6874{_}Wasn't he always snooping 'round in the regiment trying to undermine your brother?
10062-8{_}6875{_}Wasn't he always trying to be popular?
10062-8{_}6876{_}Ah, I know the Spragues.
10062-8{_}6877{_}But I'll give them a wrench that'll twist their damned pride out of them.
10062-8{_}6878{_}I'll have that cold-blooded young villain shot in a hollow square, and I'll have it done in this very district, that the whole county may know the disgrace of the high and mighty Spragues."
10062-8{_}6879{_}"No, father."
10062-8{_}6880{_}Kate had heard all this before, but she, for the first time, resolved upon setting her father right.
10062-8{_}6881{_}"No, Jack hasn't a particle of the feeling you ascribe to him.
10062-8{_}6882{_}I don't think he liked poor Wesley.
10062-8{_}6883{_}They were totally unlike in nature, and I think that Jack felt deeply that he had been wronged by Wesley's appointment.
10062-8{_}6884{_}But it was not in his nature to seek revenge.
10062-8{_}6885{_}He would have fought Wesley openly, but he would never be one of a gang of murderers.
10062-8{_}6886{_}I think I can see how Jack was led into the part he played.
10062-8{_}6887{_}It does not lessen the guilt, but it relieves him of the odious suspicions I first felt."
10062-8{_}6888{_}Then Boone, in irritable impatience, reminded her of her own earlier utterances; how from his first coming Wesley had been treated with studied distrust; how he had been denied the boyish intimacy that existed between Jack and Dick; how he was insensibly made to feel that he was in the house under a different cartel from that of Jack and Dick; that he was a prisoner on parole, and his word was doubted.
10062-8{_}6889{_}Nothing could make him believe, he declared, getting up moodily, but that the whole lot of them had set out to drive Wesley into a corner and then kill him, as they had done.
10062-8{_}6890{_}Kate sighed wearily as her father left the room.
10062-8{_}6891{_}If she could only be as well assured as her strong words implied!
10062-8{_}6892{_}Ah!
10062-8{_}6893{_}if she could fetch back her lover by getting at the truth, how willingly she would fly to Rosedale and learn all!
10062-8{_}6894{_}But she dared not question, lest questioning should confirm, where she now at least had the miserable solace of doubt.
10062-8{_}6895{_}Could it be true?
10062-8{_}6896{_}Could Jack be the base schemer her father depicted him?
10062-8{_}6897{_}Then her mind ran back to Rosedale.
10062-8{_}6898{_}She lived again all the enchanting days of that earthly paradise.
10062-8{_}6899{_}She saw Wesley's furtive starts, his strange disappearances, his growing melancholy, his moody reticence when she questioned him.
10062-8{_}6900{_}Ah!
10062-8{_}6901{_}if he had but confided to her!
10062-8{_}6902{_}If she had but dreamed of the desperate purpose born of the loneliness he lived in!
10062-8{_}6903{_}If Jack had been loyal to him, loyal to her, Wesley would have been warned that eager eyes were upon him, ready wits reading his purposes, and revengeful hatred ready to slaughter him.
10062-8{_}6904{_}When the news came that Jack had lost his life in the very enterprise Wesley had contemplated, Kate collapsed under the shock.
10062-8{_}6905{_}Now, when it was too late, she convinced herself that he was innocent.
10062-8{_}6906{_}If she could have recalled him to life, she cried in self-reproach, she would not ask whether he was all her first impulse had painted him.
10062-8{_}6907{_}She had borne up with something like composure when Wesley's death came upon her; but now, tortured by a sense of responsibility in Jack's fate, she gave way to the grief she had so long repressed.
10062-8{_}6908{_}If she had not upbraided him, if she had not accused him, in so many words, of murder, he would never have embarked on the mad plot of escape.
10062-8{_}6909{_}She had driven him to his death.
10062-8{_}6910{_}She had sat silent while Acredale rang with calumnies against him.
10062-8{_}6911{_}It was not too late yet to make reparation.
10062-8{_}6912{_}She would proclaim publicly that her brother had rashly courted his own death; that Jack had unknowingly shot him down, as many a man does, in battle, shoot his best friend.
10062-8{_}6913{_}She resolved on the instant to go to the stricken family and make such expiation there as was in her power.
10062-8{_}6914{_}But was there any certainty that the report of Jack's death was true?
10062-8{_}6915{_}Grievous mistakes of the same sort had been made repeatedly in the public journals.
10062-8{_}6916{_}She was not able to formulate any plan at first.
10062-8{_}6917{_}Her father was more morose than ever.
10062-8{_}6918{_}He seemed in his way to deplore the young man's death, but not in pity, as she soon learned.
10062-8{_}6919{_}Death had robbed him of a cruelly meditated revenge.
10062-8{_}6920{_}She wisely made no comment when this brutal feeling betrayed itself; but for the first time in her life the girl shuddered at the sight of her father.
10062-8{_}6921{_}The vague rumors of years, that had been whispered about him--rumors which of old had fired her soul with hot indignation, came back insidiously.
10062-8{_}6922{_}She shuddered.
10062-8{_}6923{_}Was she to lose all--brother, lover, father--in this unnatural strife?
10062-8{_}6924{_}She had been so loyal to her father.
10062-8{_}6925{_}She had been so proud of him when others reviled.
10062-8{_}6926{_}She had felt so serenely confident of the nobleness of his heart, the generosity of his impulses.
10062-8{_}6927{_}She had always been able to mold him, as she thought.
10062-8{_}6928{_}Could it be possible that he was human to her, inhuman to the rest of the world?
10062-8{_}6929{_}Then her mind, tortured by newly awakened doubts, ran back over the events leading to the rupture with the Spragues.
10062-8{_}6930{_}She groaned at the retrospect.
10062-8{_}6931{_}It was injustice that had displaced Jack in the command of the company.
10062-8{_}6932{_}It was injustice that had marked her father's conduct in the Perley feud.
10062-8{_}6933{_}Grief is a logician of very direct methods.
10062-8{_}6934{_}Its clarifying processes work like light in darkness.
10062-8{_}6935{_}Kate saw the past in her father's conduct with terrifying vividness.
10062-8{_}6936{_}She realized that it was her father's harsh purpose that had arrayed Acredale against him.
10062-8{_}6937{_}It was his pride and arrogant obstinacy that had brought about the loss of all she loved.
10062-8{_}6938{_}The fates had immolated the helpless; were the fates preparing a still bitterer expiation?
10062-8{_}6939{_}Life had very little left for her now, but she resolved that she would no longer be isolated by her father's enmities.
10062-8{_}6940{_}The great house had been gloomy enough for father and daughter during the last miserable months, but he still fled to her for comfort.
10062-8{_}6941{_}It was one evening when he came in, apparently in better spirits than he had shown since Wesley's death, that she told him what had been filling her mind since Jack's death.
10062-8{_}6942{_}"O father, I think I see that our lives have been unworthy, if not altogether wrong.
10062-8{_}6943{_}Surely such neighbors as ours could not all take sides against you, if you were in the right in all the feuds that have divided us as a family from the people of Acredale."
10062-8{_}6944{_}Then, in an almost imploring tone of reproach, she retraced the harsh episodes in the father's dealings with the Perleys, with the community, and, finally, the quarrel with the Spragues, involving in it the lives of Wesley and Jack.
10062-8{_}6945{_}Her voice softened into tremulousness.
10062-8{_}6946{_}She arose, and in her old pleading way pulled the shaggy head down on her breast, pressing her lips on the high, bare forehead.
10062-8{_}6947{_}"Dear father, all this is unchristian; you have in reality been waging war against women and children.
10062-8{_}6948{_}Jack was a mere boy, Richard is a boy.
10062-8{_}6949{_}I don't go into other enmities, where you have used the enormous power of wealth to crush the helpless.
10062-8{_}6950{_}If you had not alienated the Spragues and encouraged Wesley in overbearing Jack, my brother would be alive to-day.
10062-8{_}6951{_}My sweetheart--yes, Jack was dearer than all the world to me--he would not be dead to-day.
10062-8{_}6952{_}Ah!
10062-8{_}6953{_}father, father, what good comes of anger--what joy of revenge?
10062-8{_}6954{_}You have brought about the death of these two boys.
10062-8{_}6955{_}Is it not time to look at life with a new heart--with clear-seeing eyes?"
10062-8{_}6956{_}Elisha Boone sat quite still.
10062-8{_}6957{_}He had listened at first with a flush of anger, which deepened as the girl pleaded, until it died away and left his face very pale.
10062-8{_}6958{_}He pushed himself away from the clinging figure, as if the better to see her face.
10062-8{_}6959{_}Then his head drooped.
10062-8{_}6960{_}He sighed heavily, rose and without a word left the room.
10062-8{_}6961{_}Kate heard him ascending the stairs, then the sound of his room door softly closing.
10062-8{_}6962{_}Had the hateful fires of vengeance been quenched?
10062-8{_}6963{_}It was her father's way, when resolutely opposed, to quit the scene and without confessing himself in the wrong, do as Kate urged.
10062-8{_}6964{_}The next morning he was gone before she reached the breakfast-table.
10062-8{_}6965{_}There was a note on her plate in his handwriting.
10062-8{_}6966{_}She read with a sinking heart:  "MY DAUGHTER: If what you said last night is true, you can not be the daughter to me that you have been.
10062-8{_}6967{_}I am going to Washington, and when I come back you will know that your brother was deliberately murdered, and that his murderer, even in the grave, is held guilty before all men of the crime."
10062-8{_}6968{_}The servant confirmed the tidings.
10062-8{_}6969{_}Her father had arisen early and departed on the first train.
10062-8{_}6970{_}What could it mean?
10062-8{_}6971{_}Had he some evidence that she had not heard?
10062-8{_}6972{_}Had Jack left papers incriminating him?
10062-8{_}6973{_}Ah!
10062-8{_}6974{_}why carry the hideous feud further?
10062-8{_}6975{_}Why blast the melancholy repose of the living, by fastening this stain upon the dead?
10062-8{_}6976{_}But they could not.
10062-8{_}6977{_}She knew it.
10062-8{_}6978{_}She could herself refute any proof brought forward.
10062-8{_}6979{_}She would tell all.
10062-8{_}6980{_}She would reveal their tender relationship, and surely then any one, knowing the young man's nature, would scout the assertion of his willfully shooting Wesley.
10062-8{_}6981{_}But surely Olympia and Mrs. Sprague must be able to tell, and tell decisively, the circumstances in the tragedy.
10062-8{_}6982{_}She would go to them.
10062-8{_}6983{_}She owed this to the living; she owed it still more imperatively to the dead.
10062-8{_}6984{_}She had not seen Olympia since her return.
10062-8{_}6985{_}Mrs. Sprague had been too infirm to see her when she called.
10062-8{_}6986{_}But she would not heed rebuffs now.
10062-8{_}6987{_}In such a cause, on such a mission, she would have stood at the Sprague door a suppliant until even the obstinacy of her father would have relented.
10062-8{_}6988{_}On her way across the square she saw Merry coming from the post.
10062-8{_}6989{_}She turned out of her way, and hurrying to the near-sighted spinster held out her hand, saying, softly:  "Ah, Miss Merry, I'm so glad to see you!
10062-8{_}6990{_}I have been meaning to call on you ever since I heard of your return, but, what with sorrow and illness, I have put it off, and now I want you to take me home with you.
10062-8{_}6991{_}Will you not?"
10062-8{_}6992{_}The pleading tone, the caressing clasp of the hand, the sadly changed face, the somber black weeds, made the voice and figure so much unlike the old Kate, that Merry stood for an instant confused and blushing as she stammered:  "Bless me, Miss Kate, I--I--shouldn't have known you.
10062-8{_}6993{_}Ah, I am very glad to see you; sisters will be very glad to see you, too.
10062-8{_}6994{_}Do, do come right along with me.
10062-8{_}6995{_}I'm afraid the parlor won't be very sightly, but you won't mind, will you?"
10062-8{_}6996{_}Kate squeezed the hand still resting in her own, and drawing the long veil back over face, she walked silently with the puzzled spinster, unable to broach the theme she had at heart.
10062-8{_}6997{_}Merry spared her the torture of going at it obliquely.
10062-8{_}6998{_}"I have just been at the Spragues.
10062-8{_}6999{_}Poor dears, they are in dreadful distress.
10062-8{_}7000{_}Mrs. Sprague is preparing to go in search of the body, but Olympia won't give in that Jack is killed.
10062-8{_}7001{_}She says that if he had been she certainly would have known it in Richmond, for there are couriers twice a day from the rebel outposts to the capital; that the Atterburys had taken special measures to learn the fate of the escaped prisoners; that, besides this, several young men in Richmond, who knew Jack well, had been sent down the peninsula with the prisoners, to befriend him in case he were retaken."
10062-8{_}7002{_}"And Olympia believes that Jack is alive?"
10062-8{_}7003{_}"Yes, firmly."
10062-8{_}7004{_}"Where does she think he is?"
10062-8{_}7005{_}"She believes that he is among a squad separated from the rest of the prisoners, near the Union lines.
10062-8{_}7006{_}It was asserted in Richmond that many had crossed the James River, and were making for the Dismal Swamp, or into Burnside's lines in North Carolina."
10062-8{_}7007{_}"Dear Miss Merry, I--I--think I won't go in now," Kate said, tremblingly.
10062-8{_}7008{_}"I must see Olympia.
10062-8{_}7009{_}Perhaps I can help them in the search for Jack, and you know there is no time to lose.
10062-8{_}7010{_}I shall come and see you all soon."
10062-8{_}7011{_}She squeezed the astonished Merry's hand, convulsively, and shot off, leaving the bewildered lady quite speechless, so speechless that, when she reached the stately presence of Aunt Pliny, she forgot the commissions she had been sent to execute, and was at once reviled by the parrot as "a no-account dawdler."
10062-8{_}7012{_}Meanwhile, Kate, with wild, throbbing hope in her heart that kindled color in her pale cheeks and light in her weary eyes, sped away to the Spragues.
10062-8{_}7013{_}There was no tremor in the hand that raised the dragon-headed knocker, nor hesitancy in the voice that bade the servant say that "Miss Boone requested a few moments' conversation with Miss Sprague."
10062-8{_}7014{_}Olympia came presently into the reception-room, and the girls met with a warm embrace.
10062-8{_}7015{_}"Ah, Olympia, I have been made so--so--glad by what Merry tells me!
10062-8{_}7016{_}You--do--not believe that your brother is dead?"
10062-8{_}7017{_}Her voice faltered, and Olympia, gazing at her fixedly, said:  "No, I shall not believe Jack is dead until I see his body.
10062-8{_}7018{_}Poor mother, who believes the worst whenever we are out of her sight, has given up all but the faintest hope.
10062-8{_}7019{_}I shall not.
10062-8{_}7020{_}I know Jack so well.
10062-8{_}7021{_}I know that it would take a good deal to kill him, young and strong as he is.
10062-8{_}7022{_}Besides that, I know that the Atterburys would find means to let us know, if there were any certainty as to his fate.
10062-8{_}7023{_}Poor Jack!
10062-8{_}7024{_}It would be an unendurable calamity if he were to die before the monstrous calumnies that have been published about him are proved lies."
10062-8{_}7025{_}"Dear Olympia, that is one reason of my coming.
10062-8{_}7026{_}In my horror at Rosedale, I, too, believed that John had been in a plot to entrap Wesley; but I--I--know better now, and I have come to tell you that it is no less my duty than my right to see that your brother's memory is made as spotless as his life."
10062-8{_}7027{_}"I knew it; I knew you would, do it; I told Jack so in Richmond, almost the last words I said before he set out on this miserable adventure.
10062-8{_}7028{_}I told him you were not the girl I took you for if you could believe him to be such a dastard, when you had time to get over the shock of poor Wesley's death.
10062-8{_}7029{_}You never heard the whole story of that dreadful night.
10062-8{_}7030{_}I must tell it to you--as he would if he were here, and I know you would believe him."
10062-8{_}7031{_}The two girls sat down, hand in hand, and Olympia told the tale as it has been set down in these pages.
10062-8{_}7032{_}Kate was sobbing when the story ended.
10062-8{_}7033{_}She flung her arms about Olympia's neck, and for a time the two sat silent, tearful.
10062-8{_}7034{_}"Oh, why didn't he tell me this at the time?
10062-8{_}7035{_}It was not Jack's bullet that entered poor Wesley's body.
10062-8{_}7036{_}Jack was at his right, at the side of the bed.
10062-8{_}7037{_}Wesley's wound was on the left side, and the shot must have come from Jones's pistol!"
10062-8{_}7038{_}"I remember that; but Jack's remorse put all thought of everything else out of my head.
10062-8{_}7039{_}I recall, perfectly, that the wound was in Wesley's left side.
10062-8{_}7040{_}Oh, if I could only get that word to Jack!
10062-8{_}7041{_}I If--"  "I'll get it to him if he's alive.
10062-8{_}7042{_}I, or mine, have been his undoing!
10062-8{_}7043{_}I shall make amends.
10062-8{_}7044{_}Ah, Olympia, I--I am ashamed to feel so full of joy--forgive me."
10062-8{_}7045{_}"It isn't your fault, dear, that you didn't know Jack as we do," Olympia said, tenderly.
10062-8{_}7046{_}"What are your plans?"
10062-8{_}7047{_}Kate asked, presently.
10062-8{_}7048{_}"Mother insists upon going to the peninsula and examining the ground, questioning all who took part in the pursuit, and seeing with her own eyes every wounded man in the neighborhood.
10062-8{_}7049{_}I don't know whether we can get passes, but we shall set out at once and do our best."
10062-8{_}7050{_}"O Olympia.
10062-8{_}7051{_}I must--I must go with you!
10062-8{_}7052{_}I shall die if I remain here doing nothing--helpless!
10062-8{_}7053{_}Let me go.
10062-8{_}7054{_}I can aid you much.
10062-8{_}7055{_}I can surely get all the passports required.
10062-8{_}7056{_}I can do many things that you couldn't do, for my father--"  She stopped and colored.
10062-8{_}7057{_}Her father!
10062-8{_}7058{_}What was she rashly promising for him?
10062-8{_}7059{_}Dead, he was bent on Jack's dishonor; living, he would never rest until Jack's life was condemned.
10062-8{_}7060{_}"Ah, yes--that's true.
10062-8{_}7061{_}Your father is potent at headquarters.
10062-8{_}7062{_}I can answer for mamma.
10062-8{_}7063{_}We shall be delighted and comforted to have you.
10062-8{_}7064{_}I shall need you as much as mamma needs me.
10062-8{_}7065{_}We are only waiting for Mr. Brodie's report.
10062-8{_}7066{_}I don't expect much from his researches.
10062-8{_}7067{_}It is only a woman's heart that upholds one in such trials as this search means."
10062-8{_}7068{_}The plans were agreed upon at once and the two girls separated, knit together by the same bond in more senses than one, for, while Olympia set out to rescue her brother, she secretly hoped that the search would bring her near some one else; and so, as soon as Kate had gone, she sat down and wrote Vincent of Jack's disappearance, asking his aid in finding such traces as might be in the rebel lines.
10062-8{_}7069{_}She merely alluded to their projected plan, adding, in a postscript, that she would write him as soon as the party approached the outposts.
10062-8{_}7070{_}Kate wrote at once to her father, at his Washington address, narrating her visit to the Spragues, telling him of the new hope that had come to her, and beseeching him to lend his whole heart to the distressed mother and sister.
10062-8{_}7071{_}He should see her in Washington within a few days, and she counted on his sympathy with her to help to restore the lost son and brother if alive, to co-operate in giving the body honorable burial if he were dead.
10062-8{_}7072{_}These letters dispatched, the party waited only to hear from Brodie.
10062-8{_}7073{_}He came a day or two later, but he could give them no hope.
10062-8{_}7074{_}He had been repelled from all sources of information, insulted in the War Office, and denied access to the President.
10062-8{_}7075{_}He was convinced that there were secret influences at work to obscure the true facts in the case of the escaped prisoners, but what the agencies were he could not guess.
10062-8{_}7076{_}When Olympia told this to Kate, she was surprised at her look and response.
10062-8{_}7077{_}"I know the influences, I think, and I can discover the agencies.
10062-8{_}7078{_}Take comfort.
10062-8{_}7079{_}I believe Jack is alive.
10062-8{_}7080{_}I promise you that I shall never rest until he is found, alive or dead."
10062-8{_}7081{_}"O Kate, what an impulsive ally we have gained!
10062-8{_}7082{_}I wish Jack could have heard that speech; it would have put power in his arm, as poor Barney used to say."
10062-8{_}7083{_}Twenty-four hours later the three women were in Washington, Kate remaining with her friends, instead of joining her father at Willard's.
10062-8{_}7084{_}CHAPTER XXX.
10062-8{_}7085{_}A GAME OF CHANCE.
10062-8{_}7086{_}It was the end of January, 1862, when Olympia and her mother found themselves in Washington for the second time in quest of the missing soldier.
10062-8{_}7087{_}They took lodgings in the same quiet house, not far from Lafayette Square--Kate with them.
10062-8{_}7088{_}Kate counted upon her father's aid, active or passive; but when her messenger returned from Willard's with word that Mr. Boone had gone from the hotel several days before, she was numb with a dreadful foreboding.
10062-8{_}7089{_}He was avoiding her deliberately.
10062-8{_}7090{_}She drove at once to the hotel.
10062-8{_}7091{_}The clerk summoned to her aid could only inform her that her father had given up his room and had left the hotel late at night.
10062-8{_}7092{_}She could get no further clew.
10062-8{_}7093{_}She telegraphed at once to Acredale and returned to the Spragues, not daring to breathe her apprehensions.
10062-8{_}7094{_}Yes, her father was plainly keeping away from her.
10062-8{_}7095{_}He meant to persist in his savage vengeance.
10062-8{_}7096{_}What had he learned?
10062-8{_}7097{_}Was Jack indeed dead, and was his good name the object of her father's hatred?
10062-8{_}7098{_}Whither should she turn?
10062-8{_}7099{_}Why had she not thought of this--her fathers passivity or even opposition?
10062-8{_}7100{_}How could she reveal her terrors to the mother and sister?
10062-8{_}7101{_}How make known to them the unworthy side of her father's character?
10062-8{_}7102{_}If in the morning no telegram came from Acredale, it would be proof that her father was bent, implacably in his purpose to undo Jack, living or dead.
10062-8{_}7103{_}When she reached the lodging, Olympia was dressed for the street.
10062-8{_}7104{_}"You are just in time.
10062-8{_}7105{_}I have matured my plans.
10062-8{_}7106{_}First, we must find out at the proper quarter the names of all the wounded brought here from Fort Monroe.
10062-8{_}7107{_}Then we must trace the report in the _Herald_ down to its origin.
10062-8{_}7108{_}Then we must visit every hospital in and near Washington to find out from actual sight of each man whether Jack or Dick, or any one we know, is in the city.
10062-8{_}7109{_}As we go on, we shall learn a good deal which may modify this plan, or perhaps make the search less difficult."
10062-8{_}7110{_}Olympia said this with composure and a certain confidence in herself that struck Kate with admiration.
10062-8{_}7111{_}She felt ashamed of herself.
10062-8{_}7112{_}Here was Olympia, unconscious of Jack's real peril if living, the menace to his reputation if dead, planning as composedly as if it were an every-day thing to have a brother lost in the appalling mazes of war; and she had been weakly depending upon her father, Jack's most persevering enemy!
10062-8{_}7113{_}She recoiled from herself in a shiver of self-reproach as she said:  "Olympia, you have the good sense of a man in an emergency.
10062-8{_}7114{_}I am ashamed of myself.
10062-8{_}7115{_}I, who ought to do the thinking for you, am as helpless as a kitchen-maid set to playing lady in the parlor.
10062-8{_}7116{_}I can at least help you; I can make my body follow you, if I haven't sense enough to suggest."
10062-8{_}7117{_}"Dear Kate, it isn't sense, or insight, or any fine quality of mind that is needed here.

10062-8{_}7119{_}Poor mamma!
10062-8{_}7120{_}She is as easily influenced as a baby.
10062-8{_}7121{_}Jack is her darling, remember.
10062-8{_}7122{_}All the world is a small affair to her compared with our poor boy.

10062-8{_}7124{_}But Kate could stand no more of this.

10062-8{_}7133{_}The White House was gay with hunting, and salutes from the distant forts were signalizing the news that had just come of Union successes at Mill Spring and Roanoke Island.
10062-8{_}7134{_}The girls, procuring a hack, were driven to the provost-general's office.

10062-8{_}7138{_}"It is more than likely that these names are wrong.
10062-8{_}7139{_}This happens constantly.
10062-8{_}7140{_}The operators are raw and some of them can barely read.
10062-8{_}7141{_}The names are given hurriedly, and if not written plainly they make wretched work of them.
10062-8{_}7142{_}The newspapers make many a fool famous, while neglecting many a hero who deserves fame, simply through the blundering or carelessness of the writers or operators.
10062-8{_}7143{_}Here is an orderly who will take you to the surgeon-general.
10062-8{_}7144{_}You will find in his books the names of all the wounded in hospital in the Eastern armies.
10062-8{_}7145{_}But if your brother was wounded or brought in wounded at Fort Monroe, his name will be on the books of the Army of the Potomac or the Department of Eastern Virginia."
10062-8{_}7146{_}They were treated with the same deferential gallantry at the surgeon-general's office; the young doctors, indeed, became almost obtrusive in their eagerness to spare the young women the drudgery of scrutinizing the long lists of invalids.
10062-8{_}7147{_}But, after two days' careful search, no names resembling Sprague or Perley could be found.
10062-8{_}7148{_}"I wonder who this can be?"
10062-8{_}7149{_}Kate said, returning to an entry made a month before: "Jones, Warchester; Caribee Regiment."

10062-8{_}7151{_}Let us go to him.
10062-8{_}7152{_}It will do no harm to find out who he is."
10062-8{_}7153{_}The surgeon's clerk readily gave them Jones's address, reminding them that the hospital was in Georgetown, and that they would be too late to obtain entrance to the patient that day.
10062-8{_}7154{_}Next morning Mrs. Sprague was too ill to rise from her bed, and Olympia could not leave her alone.
10062-8{_}7155{_}Kate undertook the investigation into the Jones affair alone.
10062-8{_}7156{_}When she reached the hospital there was some delay before she could see the personage intrusted with the admission of guests.
10062-8{_}7157{_}She was shown into an office on the ground-floor and given a seat.

10062-8{_}7159{_}He would have him moved, and the surgeon-general gave him _carte blanche_ with the patient."

10062-8{_}7167{_}Whom had her father been taking from the hospital--Jack?

10062-8{_}7228{_}Jones, sent from Hampton Hospital, December 13th.
10062-8{_}7229{_}This was about the time Jack had reached the Union lines.
10062-8{_}7230{_}He had left Richmond late in November.
10062-8{_}7231{_}All Brodie's inquiries at Fort Monroe had been fruitless in finding the whereabouts of the fugitives that came through the lines at that time.
10062-8{_}7232{_}Dick had been one of them.
10062-8{_}7233{_}If Jones were not Jack himself, he must have been one of the group that escaped with Jack.
10062-8{_}7234{_}It all led back to the first frightful conjecture.
10062-8{_}7235{_}Her father was abducting a witness who could divulge Jack's whereabouts, or he was secreting Jack until be could work him harm.
10062-8{_}7236{_}The walk began to revive Kate's courage as well as her faculties.

10062-8{_}7318{_}The regiment, or what was left of it, was home refilling its ranks.

10062-8{_}7356{_}He could be found in the military hospital in Warchester.

10062-8{_}7367{_}"Oh no, miss.
10062-8{_}7368{_}Jones wa'nt brought here; he was took to a private place.

10062-8{_}7384{_}Kate began to breathe more freely.
10062-8{_}7385{_}Her father had, at least, avoided any collusion with inferiors.
10062-8{_}7386{_}His handiwork had been natural, involving no conspiracy or bribing of menials.
10062-8{_}7387{_}"Do you think you could find out for me where Mr. Jones is?"
10062-8{_}7388{_}"Wall, I reckon it could be done.
10062-8{_}7389{_}It may take some days, as I must trust to the luck of running upon old Dofunny again."
10062-8{_}7390{_}Kate started.
10062-8{_}7391{_}"Old Dofunny"--the unsuspecting humorist meant her father by this jocular _nom de guerre_, and she dared not resent it.
10062-8{_}7392{_}How should she gain her end and yet save herself from the humiliation of seeming to spy upon her father?
10062-8{_}7393{_}It wouldn't do for Elkins to go to him, for he would at once suspect, inquire, and learn that she had come upon his tracks.
10062-8{_}7394{_}If she could only see him face to face, she would be spared all this odious complotting.
10062-8{_}7395{_}But she dared not reject the means Providence had put in her hands.
10062-8{_}7396{_}And yet, how use them, and avoid throwing suspicion upon her father in cautioning Elkins not to approach him?
10062-8{_}7397{_}She was not equal to the invention of a plan on the moment, and said in a doubting, reflective way:  "Never mind.
10062-8{_}7398{_}I may be able to learn from some of his friends where he is.
10062-8{_}7399{_}The gentleman you speak of does not live in this city, and you would hardly be able to find him.
10062-8{_}7400{_}If I could, find him I could find Mr.
10062-8{_}7401{_}Jones."
10062-8{_}7402{_}"Ah, yes; jes' so.
10062-8{_}7403{_}Wall, I think I can find him in another way.
10062-8{_}7404{_}I remember the carriage that took him from the station, I can find out from the driver.
10062-8{_}7405{_}'T'wan't no mystery, I reckon."
10062-8{_}7406{_}Kate looked into the innocent blue eyes as the young fellow scratched his tow head, wondering whether he was as simple-minded as he seemed.
10062-8{_}7407{_}He stood the scrutiny with blushing restiveness, in which there was nothing of the malign, and she resolved that he was to be trusted.
10062-8{_}7408{_}"Very well," she said, indifferently, "that does seem the shortest way to find out the poor fellow's whereabouts.
10062-8{_}7409{_}Get the facts, and you shall be well paid for your trouble."
10062-8{_}7410{_}"'Tain't no trouble, miss, if it's a service to you.
10062-8{_}7411{_}It would make me powerful glad to do anything for a comrade or his sister."
10062-8{_}7412{_}Kate smiled at the astute mingling of sly fun and questioning implied in the gently rising inflection in this query.
10062-8{_}7413{_}"Yes," she said, "you will be relieving the anxious heart of a sister if you find what I am seeking."
10062-8{_}7414{_}"Nuff said, miss.
10062-8{_}7415{_}Just as soon as I get my relief I'm off like a shot.
10062-8{_}7416{_}Where shall you be?"
10062-8{_}7417{_}"Ah, yes; you can come to me at the Alburn House.
10062-8{_}7418{_}Here is my card, and you will doubtless be at some expense.
10062-8{_}7419{_}Here is money to pay--spare no expense."
10062-8{_}7420{_}The big eyes opened in wonder as Kate handed him three new ten-dollar greenbacks, just then something of a novelty to soldiers especially, who got their pay infrequently.
10062-8{_}7421{_}It was a bold stroke to intrust her name to this unconscious agent of her father, for, if he were really playing a part, his first act would be to reveal her visit and thus set her father on his guard.
10062-8{_}7422{_}But she trusted him implicitly.
10062-8{_}7423{_}His wide-open blue eyes, the artless admiration mingling with his bashful diffidence, all were proof that he could not be deceiving her.
10062-8{_}7424{_}She took rooms at the Alburn House, which was not the chief hotel, as being better adapted for her purpose of seclusion.
10062-8{_}7425{_}At the big hotel she was known, and if her father were in town she would be under his espionage without the solace of writing him.
10062-8{_}7426{_}Late in the evening her agent came in radiant.
10062-8{_}7427{_}He had found the man.
10062-8{_}7428{_}"Easy as rolling off a log."
10062-8{_}7429{_}The hackman had taken him to the house where Jones was lying.
10062-8{_}7430{_}It was on the outskirts of the city toward Acredale.
10062-8{_}7431{_}He described the house.
10062-8{_}7432{_}Kate knew it very well.
10062-8{_}7433{_}It was the property of her father.
10062-8{_}7434{_}"Did you see the patient?"
10062-8{_}7435{_}"No, indeed.
10062-8{_}7436{_}You didn't tell me to, and I had nothing, to see him for.
10062-8{_}7437{_}Ef you had told me that you wanted I should see him, I'd have seen him as easy as greased lightning."
10062-8{_}7438{_}"Thank you.
10062-8{_}7439{_}I am relieved of a great burden through your kindness.
10062-8{_}7440{_}You must permit me to give you something to show my gratitude.
10062-8{_}7441{_}Here, use this money for some one who needs it, if you do not need it yourself."
10062-8{_}7442{_}"But I don't need it.
10062-8{_}7443{_}Here is what you gave me this morning, 'cept a half-dollar I spent in treating John.
10062-8{_}7444{_}I couldn't think of taking so much money.
10062-8{_}7445{_}It's more'n Uncle Sam allows me for five months' pay."
10062-8{_}7446{_}"No, I shall feel distressed if you do not accept it.
10062-8{_}7447{_}You can find use for it.
10062-8{_}7448{_}It will bring you luck, for it is the reward of a very important service.
10062-8{_}7449{_}Perhaps some time we may meet again, and then you shall know how important."
10062-8{_}7450{_}The tow hair stood up in wild dismay, and the blue eyes were perfect saucepans, as Kate gently forced the money into the big palm.
10062-8{_}7451{_}"Wall, I vum, miss, I feel like I was a-robbing you, but ef yeou deu want I should take it, why I will, and send it to my old mother, who will find plenty o' use for it.
10062-8{_}7452{_}Good-by, miss.
10062-8{_}7453{_}Ef you should want me again, I'm at the hospital.
10062-8{_}7454{_}I shall be mitey tickled to do anything for yeou or your brother."
10062-8{_}7455{_}CHAPTER XXXI.
10062-8{_}7456{_}TWO BLADES OF THE SAME STEEL.
10062-8{_}7457{_}It was too late to follow up the discovery that night.
10062-8{_}7458{_}Kate, after a feverish rest, set out early in the morning.
10062-8{_}7459{_}She went first to Acredale, where she could get her own equipage and driver.
10062-8{_}7460{_}The tenants of the house did not know her.
10062-8{_}7461{_}She rang boldly at the door, and when a maid answered, quite taken aback by the girlish figure in deep black, Kate asked, confidently:  "I want to see the sick man, Mr.
10062-8{_}7462{_}Jones."
10062-8{_}7463{_}"Yes'm, come right in.
10062-8{_}7464{_}This way, please, ma'am."
10062-8{_}7465{_}The girl led the way up a flight of stairs, but if she had been part of the balustrade Kate could not have been more immovable.
10062-8{_}7466{_}Whom was she about to see?
10062-8{_}7467{_}Jack, wan, emaciated, on the verge of the grave?
10062-8{_}7468{_}They had said in Washington that the journey would kill him; was it to that end her relentless father had persisted in the removal?
10062-8{_}7469{_}Was she about to see the dying brought to death's door by her own flesh and blood?
10062-8{_}7470{_}She reeled against the stair-post and brought her veil over her face.
10062-8{_}7471{_}The girl had turned above and was waiting in wonder.
10062-8{_}7472{_}With a desperate gathering together of her relaxed forces, she mounted the stairway.
10062-8{_}7473{_}In the corridor the girl turned to a closed doorway and knocked lightly.
10062-8{_}7474{_}There was no sound within; but the door swung open, and Elisha Boone stood on the threshold.
10062-8{_}7475{_}He did not in the dim light observe the figure in black, but, looking at the maid, said, softly:  "What's wanted, Sarah?"
10062-8{_}7476{_}"A young lady to see Mr. Jones, sir," and, stepping slightly aside for Kate to enter, the father recognized the visitor.
10062-8{_}7477{_}"You here, Kate?
10062-8{_}7478{_}What does this mean?"
10062-8{_}7479{_}With a great throb of joy she flung herself into his arms; too happy, too relieved to take into consideration the defeat of her purpose involved in the meeting.
10062-8{_}7480{_}For an instant she lost all thought of anything but that her estranged parent was in her arms, that she would not let him quit her sight again, that her pleading would keep him from any act that could cause her or any one else unhappiness.
10062-8{_}7481{_}"Ah, father, I'm so relieved, so glad!
10062-8{_}7482{_}I was miserable, and did not know where you were.
10062-8{_}7483{_}I--I will not let you leave me again."
10062-8{_}7484{_}"But my child, you must not be here; this is a house of sickness; there is dangerous illness here."
10062-8{_}7485{_}"It's no more dangerous for me than for you.
10062-8{_}7486{_}I know who is here."
10062-8{_}7487{_}She looked archly at him, as he started in surprise.
10062-8{_}7488{_}"I will help nurse Mr.
10062-8{_}7489{_}Jones."
10062-8{_}7490{_}She said this with immense knowingness in her manner as she squeezed the astonished man to her heart.
10062-8{_}7491{_}The maid meanwhile had retreated to a safe distance, where she lurked in covert to make report of the extraordinary goings on.
10062-8{_}7492{_}"Impossible, Kate; you must not be here.
10062-8{_}7493{_}I will not have it; you must go."
10062-8{_}7494{_}His voice grew stern.
10062-8{_}7495{_}"You must go, I say, Kate; you must go down-stairs this instant."
10062-8{_}7496{_}"Come, Boone, I say, this isn't fair; let the lady come in if she wants to see valor laid low."
10062-8{_}7497{_}Boone, who had been insensibly moving Kate from the open doorway, caught her eye fixed on the room, and looking over his shoulder at these jocular words he saw Jones leaning against the post, a wan smile on his face.
10062-8{_}7498{_}Boone turned, almost flinging Kate from him, and, fairly lifting the invalid, carried him back into the room.
10062-8{_}7499{_}"This is madness; you are in no condition to rise.
10062-8{_}7500{_}I won't be responsible for your life if you persist in this course."
10062-8{_}7501{_}"So much trouble off your hands, old man.
10062-8{_}7502{_}I'll be more use to you dead than living.
10062-8{_}7503{_}Better let me blow my own flame out.
10062-8{_}7504{_}It won't burn long at best or worst."
10062-8{_}7505{_}In the overwhelming revulsion of feeling brought about by the actual sight of Jones, Kate stood, interdicted, in the corridor, uncertain what to do.
10062-8{_}7506{_}She heard the man's words and shuddered at the bantering levity with which he spoke of his own death.
10062-8{_}7507{_}Who could it be?
10062-8{_}7508{_}It was not Jack, as she had feared and hoped.
10062-8{_}7509{_}But he must know something of Jack.
10062-8{_}7510{_}She must speak with him.
10062-8{_}7511{_}How?
10062-8{_}7512{_}It would not do to irritate her father.
10062-8{_}7513{_}She caught Boone's almost whispered words:  "I tell you, Jones, you shall be brought about, but you know the danger of seeing any Acredale people.
10062-8{_}7514{_}My daughter knows you--knows the Perleys.
10062-8{_}7515{_}I should think that would be reason enough why you should not be seen by her."
10062-8{_}7516{_}"Oh, I don't mind; the sight of a pretty girl is the best medicine I know of.
10062-8{_}7517{_}I'd risk all Acredale for that."
10062-8{_}7518{_}Kate turned softly and waited at the foot of the stairs for her father.
10062-8{_}7519{_}He came presently, looking worried and embarrassed.
10062-8{_}7520{_}"Now don't go to imagining mysteries here.
10062-8{_}7521{_}This is a man who has been on my hands a good many years.
10062-8{_}7522{_}He is an irreclaimable spendthrift.
10062-8{_}7523{_}He was in other days a man of repute and station.
10062-8{_}7524{_}I am interested in him, through old ties, since the days we were boys."
10062-8{_}7525{_}"The carriage is here, papa; won't you come home with me?"
10062-8{_}7526{_}"Yes; you get into the carriage."
10062-8{_}7527{_}He reappeared presently, the face of a strange woman, that Kate had not seen, peering over his shoulder into the carriage as he came down the steps.
10062-8{_}7528{_}Kate instantly divined that he had been warning the landlady against admitting strangers to the sick man's room.
10062-8{_}7529{_}During the drive home Kate strove to reassert her old dominion over the moody figure at her side.
10062-8{_}7530{_}It was useless.
10062-8{_}7531{_}As the carriage stopped at the door he turned toward her and said, not unkindly:  "Daughter, there are some things I know better how to manage than you do.
10062-8{_}7532{_}You have been spying on your father.
10062-8{_}7533{_}This is another count in the long score of grudges I owe the Sprague tribe and their scoundrel son.
10062-8{_}7534{_}Understand me clearly, my child; you must not speak of this matter again.
10062-8{_}7535{_}The whole business will soon be at an end; that end is in my hands, and no power this side the grave can alter a fact in the outcome.
10062-8{_}7536{_}You are very dear to me; you are all I have left in the world; you must trust me, and you must believe that I am doing everything for the best.
10062-8{_}7537{_}Try to think that the world is not coming to an end because I insist on having my own way for once."
10062-8{_}7538{_}Nothing but the sense of having giving hostages to good behavior rather than honor upheld Kate in the line she had marked out for herself.
10062-8{_}7539{_}She was not, in the modern sense of the word, a strong-minded young woman, this sorely beset champion of the overborne.
10062-8{_}7540{_}She hadn't even the perversity of the sex in love.
10062-8{_}7541{_}Chivalrously as she loved the lost soldier, she loved her father with that old-fashioned veneration which made her see all that he did with the moral indistinctness, without which there could not be the perfect filial devotion that makes the family a union in good report and evil.
10062-8{_}7542{_}She had not even that, by no means repellent, secondary egoism which upholds us in doing ungrateful things that abstract good may follow.
10062-8{_}7543{_}Opposition, which becomes delightful when we can call it persecution, had no charm for her.
10062-8{_}7544{_}If her father had suddenly adopted the _rôle_ of the stern parent in novels and ordered her to her chamber, Kate would have regarded it as a joke, and felt rather relieved that she could thus escape the pledge given to the Spragues.
10062-8{_}7545{_}But, as it was, she felt morally bound by her promise to Olympia; and, though she realized dimly that her instrumentality was slowly involving her father in a coil of unloveliness, she resolutely braced herself for the worst.
10062-8{_}7546{_}In spite of herself she had believed in conquering her father's severity and changing his mind.
10062-8{_}7547{_}She had rescued him from revenges quite as dear to him as this, at least so far as she understood it, forgetting that her father believed himself to be pursuing the deliberate murderer of his son.
10062-8{_}7548{_}When we have achieved a victory over our own less noble impulses and put the sophistries that misled us behind us, it is impossible to realize that others have not the same vision, the same mind as our own.
10062-8{_}7549{_}Kate had accused Jack of cold-blooded murder.
10062-8{_}7550{_}She had reasoned herself out of that hateful spirit, and, forgetting that her father had not the vital force of love to act as a fulcrum, she could not quite comprehend how difficult it was to shift the wrathful burden in his mind.
10062-8{_}7551{_}She had gone too far to recede now with honor.
10062-8{_}7552{_}Olympia had trusted her, had indeed given over into her hands the active work of finding the strangely lost clew of Jack's whereabouts.
10062-8{_}7553{_}Perhaps for her father's sake it was better that she should be the instrument.
10062-8{_}7554{_}She might be able to dissemble his intervention, shield him from obloquy--if, as she feared, he was responsible for anything doubtful.
10062-8{_}7555{_}She knew her father too well to suppose that he would flinch from any measure he had proposed to himself.
10062-8{_}7556{_}She knew that she need not count any further upon her accustomed powers of persuasion.
10062-8{_}7557{_}His own words were final on that score.
10062-8{_}7558{_}If she could only learn his intentions!
10062-8{_}7559{_}If she could be sure that he was ulteriorly shaping events against Jack--was acquainted with his whereabouts--she would have known exactly what to do.
10062-8{_}7560{_}But, pilloried in doubt, shackled by the dread of exposing him in some hateful malevolence which would forever disgrace him in the community, she hardly dared stir, though she felt that every hour's delay was a new peril to Jack in some way.
10062-8{_}7561{_}The more she thought of the scene of the morning, the surer she felt that Jones--or Mr. Dick, as her father sometimes called him--was in some way an instrument in the paternal scheme.
10062-8{_}7562{_}If she could but see Jones ten minutes!
10062-8{_}7563{_}Her father, she well knew, had guarded against that.
10062-8{_}7564{_}Whom could she send in her place?
10062-8{_}7565{_}Ah!
10062-8{_}7566{_}there was the double check.
10062-8{_}7567{_}She couldn't expose her father to a stranger; yet if her apprehensions were grounded on anything more substantial than fear, strangers must in time know all.
10062-8{_}7568{_}Could Merry be made use of?
10062-8{_}7569{_}No--that would not do.
10062-8{_}7570{_}The libertine tone of the invalid, his impudent allusion to herself, convinced Kate that a man must be her agent, if any one were to be.
10062-8{_}7571{_}But what man did she know?
10062-8{_}7572{_}If she sent any of the servants, her father would recognize them, and the attempt fail.
10062-8{_}7573{_}She had trusted Elkins.
10062-8{_}7574{_}He seemed an honest, incurious lad, just the one to be trusted in the business.
10062-8{_}7575{_}She could invent a fable which would satisfy his ready credulity without compromising her father.
10062-8{_}7576{_}It was plain that he was the only resource.
10062-8{_}7577{_}She dressed at once and returned to the Alburn.
10062-8{_}7578{_}Thence she dispatched a note to Elkins, begging him to call at his earliest leisure.
10062-8{_}7579{_}While waiting his return, she wrote a letter to be handed to Jones.
10062-8{_}7580{_}This was a work of no little ingenuity, forced as she was to avoid all allusion to her father and the scene of the morning.
10062-8{_}7581{_}When completed, this stroke of the conspiracy ran:      "DEAR SIR: A mother and sister who have exhausted all     official sources in vain to get trace of a lost son and brother,     John Sprague of the Caribees, have reason to believe that     you can give them a clew to his whereabouts.
10062-8{_}7582{_}Will you     therefore kindly confide in the bearer of this letter, giving     him by word of mouth such facts as will enable John     Sprague's relatives to work intelligently in the search for     him, living or dead?
10062-8{_}7583{_}"Very truly yours,      "KATHERINE BOONE."
10062-8{_}7584{_}It was hardly written when Elkins himself appeared, radiant with satisfaction and blushing like a peony under lamplight.
10062-8{_}7585{_}"Yeour note came just in th' nick o' time.
10062-8{_}7586{_}I have leave of absence for twenty-four hours, and was just goin' inter teown."
10062-8{_}7587{_}"If you can spare me the day, I have a very important matter I think you can attend to for me.
10062-8{_}7588{_}I want you to go to the sick man Jones.
10062-8{_}7589{_}You must see before entering whether he is alone or not.
10062-8{_}7590{_}I don't know how you can find out, but you can invent some way.
10062-8{_}7591{_}If you see the man who brought him from Washington, you are not to enter.
10062-8{_}7592{_}But if you find that he is not in the house, ask boldly for Jones, and when you reach him hand him this note.
10062-8{_}7593{_}He will give you an answer, and you must be careful not to lose a word, for life depends on the accuracy of your report.
10062-8{_}7594{_}I fancy that your regimentals and hospital badge can gain you admission, if, as I have reason to believe, there are orders to refuse strangers admission.
10062-8{_}7595{_}I depend on you to overcome any difficulty you may meet.
10062-8{_}7596{_}If you knew how much depends upon it, I'm sure you would not be baffled by anything less than force."
10062-8{_}7597{_}The big blue eyes were fairly bulging, like two monster morning-glories, as Elkins, putting the note carefully in his jacket pocket, said, softly:  "Ef I don't get thet 'ere letter into Jones's hands, you may have me drummed out o' camp by the mule-drivers."
10062-8{_}7598{_}"I believe you, and trust you.
10062-8{_}7599{_}I shall be here to-morrow morning early, and shall hope to hear something from you.
10062-8{_}7600{_}Good-by."
10062-8{_}7601{_}"Good-by, miss.
10062-8{_}7602{_}Just you make up your mind I am goin' to do what you command."
10062-8{_}7603{_}When she reached home she found her father in the library.
10062-8{_}7604{_}He looked at her inquiringly as she came over and kissed him.
10062-8{_}7605{_}"I have been in town all day, and am run out."
10062-8{_}7606{_}"Still plotting?"
10062-8{_}7607{_}"Yes, still plotting."
10062-8{_}7608{_}"You're wasting your time, my dear.
10062-8{_}7609{_}You'll know all you care to soon enough, if you'll just keep quiet."
10062-8{_}7610{_}"Yes; but I can't.
10062-8{_}7611{_}I want to know all you know, and I want to know it now."
10062-8{_}7612{_}"All I know wouldn't be much, according to the Spragues, who gave me my status in this town, long ago, as an ignoramus."
10062-8{_}7613{_}"Perhaps you were then, papa."
10062-8{_}7614{_}"Yes; I hadn't been schooled fifteen years by my accomplished daughter."
10062-8{_}7615{_}"A lie is truth to those who only tell the truth."
10062-8{_}7616{_}"What does that mean?"
10062-8{_}7617{_}"It's simple enough--a home-made epigram.
10062-8{_}7618{_}People who tell nothing but the truth are easiest made to believe a lie.
10062-8{_}7619{_}The Spragues had heard of you as ignorant, and believed it.
10062-8{_}7620{_}You can't blame them for that."
10062-8{_}7621{_}"I don't blame them because it was a lie.
10062-8{_}7622{_}I blame them because it was the truth.
10062-8{_}7623{_}I don't care a straw how many lies are told about me--it's the ill-natured truth I object to."
10062-8{_}7624{_}"I'm afraid that you will have a hard time in life if you like lies better than the truth."
10062-8{_}7625{_}"I didn't say that."
10062-8{_}7626{_}"Then I don't understand English."
10062-8{_}7627{_}"You don't understand me."
10062-8{_}7628{_}"Ah, yes I do, papa.
10062-8{_}7629{_}I do understand you.
10062-8{_}7630{_}I know that at this moment you are doing something that you are ashamed of--something that later you will bitterly repent.
10062-8{_}7631{_}You are carrying on now through pride what you began in wrath.
10062-8{_}7632{_}Stop where you are.
10062-8{_}7633{_}The dead can not be avenged.
10062-8{_}7634{_}That's a barbarous code.
10062-8{_}7635{_}Remember, in all the petty irritations of the past, when you have been hurt by your neighbors, you were never so triumphant as when you surprised those who injured you by a magnanimous return--"  "There, I made an agreement with you that we should not speak of these things.
10062-8{_}7636{_}I mean it.
10062-8{_}7637{_}I find that you take advantage of me.
10062-8{_}7638{_}I shall be banished from the house if you do not keep to your bargain."
10062-8{_}7639{_}Kate sighed.
10062-8{_}7640{_}She had hoped that the early banter was paving the way for a reconciliation.
10062-8{_}7641{_}She took up some work and tried to busy her hands.
